Minister Peng Answers Reporters' Questions: Seats for Communist Party and Democratic League Representatives in the National Assembly Will Be Reserved; Pacification Zone Political Affairs Conference Concludes Today

[Special Dispatch from Nanjing, 20th] The Ministry of Information held a press conference at 3:30 PM in the National Assembly Party Representatives Lounge. About 200 people attended, including Peng Xuepei, Shen Yi, Ye Gongchao, Behr, and Chinese and foreign reporters. Peng first introduced the newly appointed Mayor of Nanjing, Shen Yi, who reported on the initial administrative policies for Nanjing. Then, they answered reporters' questions, adjourning around 5:00 PM. The following is a record of Minister Peng's answers:

Question: A spokesperson for the Chinese Communist Party (CCP) stated that Nationalist troop movements in northern Shaanxi are frequent, aircraft fly over Yan'an from time to time, and the highway north of Xi'an is being actively repaired, claiming that Nationalist troops are about to attack Yan'an. Is this true?

Answer: This kind of atmosphere may be a propaganda tactic, and a harbinger of action. It has a relationship with the newly established action committee by the CCP. Yulin has been surrounded for weeks, with communication relying solely on the air force, so it must pass over Yan'an. As for repairing the highway, this is a nationwide effort, and traffic north of Xi'an cannot be excluded.

Question: Please tell us frankly, is the government planning to attack Yan'an?

Answer: The previous answer already contained a negative response.

Question: There are rumors that Chairman Chiang recently convened a meeting of high-ranking Nationalist generals from various locations, stating that the communist forces would be eliminated in five months, and communism in China would be wiped out in five years. Is this true?

Answer: This rumor may refer to the recent Pacification Zone Political Affairs Committee meeting. Premier Song and Minister Bai served as chairman and vice-chairman respectively. The task of the committee is to plan for the rehabilitation and relief in the pacification zones. Attendees included personnel from relevant central ministries and military and political officials from various pacification areas. It was not a meeting of all high-ranking generals. For example, Chief of Staff Chen did not attend. The Chairman attended the meeting to give instructions, but such speculation about the content of the instructions is not worth denying. The meeting has continued for three days and will conclude on the 21st.

Question: Do you know if Chairman Chiang exchanged documents with Zhang Junmai?

Answer: Correspondence is normal. What I can tell you is that there is a high possibility that the China Democratic Socialist Party (MinSheDang) will attend the National Assembly. Looking back to the establishment of the first National Political Council in 1938, the members included those without party affiliation, with the Kuomintang (Nationalist Party), the Communist Party, the China Youth Party and the MinSheDang (then known as the National Socialist Party) as the main constituents. Subsequently, the Democratic League was established, mainly composed of the Youth Party and the MinSheDang, mixed with educational groups and a few individuals. The current situation is similar to that of 1938. Only the Communist Party opposes participation in the National Assembly. We are very pleased with the participation of the educational sector, non-affiliated individuals, and Mongolian compatriots in the National Assembly to jointly draft the constitution, and the delegates welcome them.

Question: Did the Democratic Governance Party led by Situ Meitang secure seats in the National Assembly?

Answer: Mr. Situ has been invited to attend the National Assembly as an overseas Chinese citizen.

Question: Since the Communist Party and the Democratic League are not participating in the National Assembly, will the government allocate their seats to other parties?

Answer: No. The seats of representatives from the Communist Party and the Democratic League will absolutely be reserved.

Question: Is the reorganization of the National Government Committee underway?

Answer: The work of various parties participating in the National Assembly has not yet been completed.

Question: There is a proposal among the National Assembly representatives to move the capital to Peiping (Beijing). It is said that the Nanjing City Councilors opposed this after listening to the proposal and are preparing to march in protest. Is this true?

Answer: I have not heard this news. Chairman Chen Yusheng has never mentioned this matter. (Speeches by Ye Gongchao and Shen Yi can be found on page two.)

Sino-British Trade Treaty Under Negotiation; Our Side is Studying the Draft; Government Has Not Yet Taken Over Dalian City

Ye Gongchao Answers Reporters' Questions

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 20th] Ye Gongchao, Director of the European Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, reported on the latest developments at a press conference with Chinese and foreign reporters this afternoon, regarding the Sino-British trade negotiations and the implementation negotiations of the Sino-French-Vietnamese agreement. The questions and answers are recorded as follows:

Question: A Peiping dispatch reported that Soviet troops have withdrawn from Dalian and that the city has been taken over by Chinese Communist troops. Have the Soviet troops withdrawn? What is the situation in Dalian? What news does the Chinese government have?

Answer: Regarding this matter, the Chinese government has not received any reports. The Soviet government notified our country on May 23rd of this year, stating that the Soviet troops had completed their withdrawal from the Northeast on May 3rd. Since that time, Soviet troops should no longer be stationed in Dalian, as the Sino-Soviet treaty signed last August does not allow the Soviet Union to station troops in Dalian. The area near Dalian is still occupied by communist troops, and the Chinese government has not taken over Dalian, so we have no further news.

Question: What is the situation regarding the Sino-British trade negotiations?

Answer: Regarding the Sino-British negotiations for a trade treaty and related agreements, the British side submitted an initial draft to the Chinese government six months ago. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is currently studying the draft. Some clauses in the draft involve other relevant government departments, and all parties are studying the relevant clauses. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs hopes to complete this draft by the end of this month, but because it is so broad, it may take a little longer. However, both the Chinese and British governments hope that the agreement can be completed as soon as possible.

Question: Regarding the Sino-French-Vietnamese negotiations, the previous Yunnan Provincial Assembly put forward six points. How is the implementation negotiation of the Sino-French-Vietnamese agreement progressing?

Answer: The Sino-French negotiations can be described in four key points: (1) Recovering the Yunnan section of the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway is a consistent policy of the government. The government has always valued the opinions of all parties in diplomatic negotiations, and the opinions of the Yunnan Provincial Assembly are naturally valued by the government. (2) The issue of Haiphong Port as a free port is being negotiated with the French side. Progress has been made, and absolute success is expected. (3) Compensation for losses of public and private materials crossing the border during the war is being negotiated. Because it involves investigation, valuation, and currency value determination, it will take a longer time. (4) Regarding the protection of overseas Chinese, the government is paying close attention. At the same time, the government is negotiating with both France and Vietnam. Once the negotiations are successful, overseas Chinese will not only be protected after implementation but will also enjoy better treatment than before. This can be stated with certainty.

Shen Yi Reports on Nanjing's Administrative Policy at Press Conference; Implementing Principles of Focusing on the Big Picture and Starting with the Small Details

[Special Dispatch from Nanjing, 20th] At a press conference held by the Ministry of Information, Nanjing Mayor Shen Yi reported on the initial administrative policy, stating briefly: For municipal construction, we will adhere to the principle of focusing on the big picture and starting with the small details. The big picture is to complete the general preparations for local autonomy and urban planning. The small details are to repair roads and waterways. In between are facilitating transportation and solving housing and school shortages. And the smallest details are to clean up dilapidated alleys and remote areas and even add public toilets, etc. He also said that the conditions for successful administration are the diligence and effort of municipal government staff, the sincere assistance of citizens, the understanding and support of the central government, and the guidance and supervision of public opinion. He then answered reporters' questions as follows:

Question: Is Nanjing's construction goal Chinese style, Western style, or a combination of Chinese and Western styles?

Answer: Regardless of Chinese or Western, the goal is a modernized city.

Question: What is Mayor Shen's view on the dance ban in Nanjing?

Answer: This is a very minor matter of municipal administration. Since all parties are paying attention and the Municipal Council will also discuss it, we should first listen to everyone's opinions.

Question: Nanjing's finances are difficult, and income and expenditure are not balanced. What are Mayor Shen's plans?

Answer: Thank you for your concern about the difficulty of balancing Nanjing's income and expenditure. This cannot be solved by discussing taxes alone, but we must also find a way to solve it.

Mrs. Cripps Arrives in Nanjing

Banquet for Chairman and Mrs. Chiang Tonight

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 20th] Mrs. Cripps and her party arrived in the capital at 11:40 AM on the 20th, flying from Shanghai on a special "Jianguo" plane from the China Navigation Brigade. Mrs. Cripps was slightly tired from the long journey and will host a banquet on the evening of the 21st to entertain Chairman and Mrs. Chiang. A press conference will be held on the 22nd to report her impressions of the trip.

[Central News Agency, London, 19th] The Times recently published a telegram from Shanghai from Mrs. Cripps, stating her impressions of her trip to China and expressing her strong desire to return to England to work on deepening the friendship between the two countries. Mrs. Cripps stated that the welcome she and her party received from all parts of the country exceeded anything she could have imagined. She also said that she was very pleased and surprised by the far-reaching and detailed allocation of the British United Aid to China Fund. Mrs. Cripps said: "The greatest privilege of our journey was to spend time with Chairman Chiang and Madame Chiang. The hospitality of Chairman Chiang and Madame Chiang was truly rare."

Qingdao Accepts Embezzlement Case; District Court Files Public Prosecution

[Central News Agency, Qingdao, 20th] Zhu Xiancai, a receiving commissioner of the Economic Ministry's Luyu-Jin District Commissioner's Office, colluded with Jia Ziyong, without appraisal and bidding procedures, to purchase 328,000 catties of liquor worth 500 yuan per catty at a low price of 170 yuan per catty in the name of the Economic Ministry's Luyu-Jin District Commissioner's Office from the Qingdao Alien Property Management Bureau. In addition, Wang Jianchuan, a chemical industry organizer at the office, embezzled nine boxes of inner and outer tires from the warehouse and falsely claimed they were stolen. The Qingdao District Court has now filed a public prosecution for both cases.

Hong Kong Police Kick Hawker to Death; Evidence of Guilt is Conclusive; But May Be Found Not Guilty Under British Law

[Central News Agency, Hong Kong, 19th] The case of Indian police officer Seth kicking Wang Shuixiang, a peanut hawker, to death was heard this afternoon. The courtroom was crowded with spectators and heavily guarded. Four Chinese were called to testify, one of whom testified that the defendant police officer kicked the deceased ten times after he fell to the ground. Dr. Howell of the Hong Kong Government Hospital found that Wang Shuixiang's death was due to internal bleeding and a ruptured spleen. Dr. Howell also stated that the bruises on Wang Shuixiang's body were undoubtedly caused by being kicked by the defendant's leather boots.

Based on the prosecutor's indictment and the questioning of witnesses, the defendant may be acquitted or receive only a light sentence under the protection of the British court. The prosecutor first stated that he was only presenting the facts related to the case to the court and said that there were contradictions in the testimonies of the prosecution's witnesses, but the court had to make a judgment. When questioning the police officer responsible for examining the deceased's body who testified, the prosecutor raised the question that the bruises on the deceased's body may have been caused by falling on a peanut basket. The deceased died from a ruptured spleen which had enlarged four times, and he could have been saved if he had been sent to the hospital earlier. The case was adjourned for further hearing on the afternoon of the 20th.

Hankou City Council Cables Government, Requesting Recovery of Hong Kong, Kowloon, and Macau

[Special Dispatch from Hankou, 20th] The Hankou City Council recently stated that the UK's continued occupation of Hong Kong, Kowloon, and Macau not only damages sovereignty but also violates justice and affects international security. It cabled the government authorities, urging them to recover the territories by a specific date, and cabled the city councils of all provinces and cities to advocate for a unified position.

Taipei's Big Thief Wu Shengcai Captured; One of the "Twelve Constellations," Nicknamed "Dog"; Discovered and Surrounded by Secret Agents While Watching a Movie

[Central News Agency, Taipei, 20th] Wu Shengcai, a well-known big thief in Taipei, was recently captured while watching the American detective movie "The Invisible Thief" at the Xinmin Theater. There are twelve famous big thieves in Taipei, known as the "Twelve Constellations," and Wu Shengcai is one of them, nicknamed "Dog." The nicknames of the other eleven are "Pig," "Cow," "Sheep," etc. They formed gangs and committed countless crimes. Wu Shengcai was particularly vicious. Two months ago, he confronted the military police and injured a police officer. For several days, two theaters here have been screening the upper and lower parts of "The Invisible Thief." The protagonist in the film, named "Ghost," is a shocking and unprecedented big thief who uses new scientific inventions, namely radio waves, to become invisible and commit robberies. He appears and disappears suddenly, making it impossible to see or defeat him. Wu Shengcai apparently became interested in this "American big thief" and went to the Xinmin Theater to watch the movie. Shortly after entering, he was discovered by a police station secret agent. When more than 20 military police rushed to surround and capture him, he jumped out of the theater, climbed onto the roof, and fired four shots to warn against being captured. Seeing that the military police were everywhere and there was no way to escape, he returned to the theater, took off his clothes, and hid under the seat, where he was then found. In the movie, the American big thief is ultimately electrocuted to death. He is now in prison, and it is feared that he will also face certain death.

Overseas Chinese Compatriots in Bagan Siapiapi Have Evacuated to Malaya

Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission Petitions Executive Yuan for Relief

[Special Dispatch from Nanjing, 20th] The Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission stated that approximately 2,000 refugees in the Bagan Siapiapi area have recently evacuated to the vicinity of Port Klang in Malaya. Their situation is extremely miserable, with many difficulties. It has petitioned the Executive Yuan to approve an initial allocation of US$20,000 for relief.

The United Nations Relief and Rehabilitation Administration (UNRRA) Highway Transportation Team: Over 880,000 Tons of Materials Transported in Ten Months

[News from This Paper] Since its establishment in January of this year, the UNRRA Highway Transportation Team has transported materials in various parts of China, reaching 83,000 tons by the end of last month. The team currently has 1,700 trucks, 20 amphibious vehicles, and a truck tractor team. The team's trucks have traveled over 3,840,000 miles, equivalent to circling the globe 150 times. The Transportation Team has established eight sub-districts in Shanghai, Tianjin, Qingdao, Changsha, Guangzhou, Liuzhou, and Kowloon, as well as nine regional detachments. Assistant Manager Mani Weaving praised the excellent work performance of Chinese drivers and mechanics in his work report. The team employs a total of 3,600 people, of whom 93 are UNRRA design personnel, and the rest are Chinese hired locally. In addition to vehicles regularly transporting materials, the team has more than 2,000 vehicles available for use by UNRRA and the Executive Yuan Relief and Rehabilitation Administration (ERRA). One of the team's largest current tasks is transporting materials for the Yellow River dike repair project. In March of this year, the team sent ten trucks to the project area for use. Now it has dispatched 90 trucks to transport construction materials, and it will soon send more than 100 trucks to transport flour and other UNRRA materials to the area.

Revitalizing Our Countryside

UNRRA and ERRA Send Experts to Train Farmers in the Use of New Agricultural Implements

[News from This City] In order to assist in the post-war recovery of the Chinese countryside, UNRRA and ERRA have transported various new agricultural implements to various agricultural production areas to train farmers in their use, so as to alleviate the poverty of the post-war countryside. This work began in the spring of this year in various regions of Hunan, and is now being carried out in the Hebei region. Training courses have been organized, with UNRRA and ERRA each sending specialized personnel to be responsible for the training. The agricultural experts sent by the United States are all volunteers who have come to China to serve and complete the responsibility of training Chinese farmers in the use of new agricultural implements.

The Ministry of Communications Decides to Establish a Railway Car Factory in Wuchang; Li Xuanyu is the Director of the Preparatory Office; The Factory Site Has Been Surveyed

[Special Dispatch from Hankou, 20th] It is reported that in order to meet the needs of railway construction, the Ministry of Communications has decided to establish a railway car manufacturing factory in Wuchang. A preparatory office has been established in Nanjing, and Li Xuanyu, who recently returned from the United States after studying railway affairs, has been appointed as the director. Xujiapeng has been selected as the factory site. Li recently came to Hankou and is actively carrying out preparations with Yu Bojie and others, the head of the construction preparation team. It is said that the factory will be quite large, and some of the equipment will be allocated from Japanese reparations. In addition, the Communications Inspection Team left for Hengyang this morning.

Price Increase for the Yunnan-Vietnam and Sichuan-Yunnan Railways Starting Next Month

[Special Dispatch from Kunming, 19th] After the price increases of state-owned enterprises, the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway is losing 400 million yuan per month, and the Sichuan-Yunnan Railway is also losing 200 million yuan per month. Passenger and freight transport is also becoming increasingly sluggish. A request has now been submitted to the Ministry of Communications to allow a 15% price increase starting in December, and to allow a monthly allocation of 20 million yuan to the Ge-Bi-Shi Railway Company, starting in September. In order to purchase more locomotives and exploit coal mines, the company has requested the government to allocate an additional 800 million yuan as a recovery fund.

Xinjiang Provincial Government Prohibits Military and Police from Interfering with Merchants and Travelers

[Central News Agency, Dihua, 20th] The Xinjiang Provincial Government recently stated that military and police have been arbitrarily inspecting merchants and travelers in various districts, and incidents of robbery and kidnapping have been reported. Unless they violate the peace terms and policy guidelines, local military and political authorities must not arbitrarily obstruct them. If there are any violations, the provincial government will conduct an investigation upon being reported by the people and will impose severe penalties.

Resources Committee Dispatches Personnel to Inspect Longyan Iron Mine

Drafts a Takeover Plan for Approval

[Umbrella Report from Nanjing, 20th] As Zhangjiakou has been recovered, the Preparatory Committee of the North China Iron and Steel Co., Ltd. under the Resources Committee, dispatched engineers Zhao Chengquan and Chuan Zuoxin from the Shijingshan Iron and Steel Plant to Zhangjiakou on October 29th to inspect Longyan. It is reported that the Yanchoushan Iron Mine can produce 1,000 tons of ore per day after a little tidying up. However, much of the machinery has been damaged or moved away. There are currently more than 200,000 tons of ore. The Pangjiabao Iron Mine has not yet been recovered. The company is currently drafting a takeover plan based on the inspection report and submitting it to the Resources Committee for approval.

New Conscription Law

Analysis of Key Implementation Points by the Ministry of National Defense

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 20th] The Ministry of National Defense, in order to avoid difficulties for the implementing agencies when handling conscription matters after the promulgation and implementation of the new Conscription Law by the National Government, has made the following analysis: (1) For counties and cities that have completed the investigation of men and women of conscription age, strict implementation should be carried out in accordance with Article 19 of the Conscription Law. (2) Counties and cities that have completed the investigation of men of conscription age should complete the conscription during the expedited period. Regarding the conscription years, if the conscription-age sons are insufficient to meet the allocated conscription quota, the age limit may be appropriately extended in order to avoid affecting social order. (3) Before the promulgation of the Implementing Regulations of the New Conscription Law, previous laws and regulations that do not conflict with the law are still valid. The above three items have been notified to all garrison districts across the country by the Ministry of National Defense.

Media Outlets Everywhere Unanimously Request Reduction or Exemption of Newspaper Postage and Electricity Fees

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 20th] Since the authorities increased postal and telegraphic fees by five to ten times from November 1st, newspaper businesses nationwide have suffered a serious impact. A copy of a newspaper subscribed to from other locations by airmail costs 230,000 yuan per month, causing hardship for both newspaper publishers and readers. Therefore, media circles in Wuhan, Shanghai, and the Shandong Provisional Assembly have all stated their reasons and telegraphed requests to the authorities for reductions or exemptions to benefit cultural development. Fifteen newspaper businesses in Nanjing, including Central, Heping (Peace), and Jiuguo (National Salvation), jointly submitted a petition to the Ministry of Transportation the day before yesterday, requesting that newspaper postal and telegraphic fees continue to be charged at the standard before October 31st. Meanwhile, representatives from the same industry across the country who are participating in the National Assembly are exchanging opinions and discussing methods to facilitate unified action. Chongqing Chairman's Headquarters Arranges for Unemployed Military Officers

Also, please extend the training deadline.

[Central News Agency, Chongqing, 19th] In recent days, thousands of unemployed military officers have gathered in Chongqing City, requesting the Chongqing branch of the Central Training Corps to admit them for training. The Chongqing Headquarters has therefore transferred an order to the Central Training Corps to appropriately relax the admission standards and suggested to the Ministry of National Defense that the registration and admission of unemployed military officers be extended again until the end of this year (originally scheduled to end on June 30th) so that a small number of genuine unemployed regular military officers can be admitted for training. Those who forge documents or impersonate others will be handled according to the law. Xiao Yisu, Chief of Staff of the Headquarters, convened a meeting with more than 300 unemployed military officers in Chongqing at 2:00 PM on the 19th. In addition to instructing them to wait quietly for the Central Training Corps to review their applications, he temporarily issued each officer a food allowance of 10,000 yuan and 30 catties of rice. Housing was allocated by the Fourth Supply District at the Nan'an Rehabilitation Station for temporary residence. The officers expressed satisfaction with these measures by the authorities and have left the urban area in groups to wait for review on the Nan'an.

Military Personnel Must Not Interfere with Road Administration

Orders from the Ministry of National Defense to pay attention

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 20th] The Ministry of National Defense stated that during the War of Resistance, various transportation arteries suffered numerous damages from military conflicts. Although active repairs were carried out after the victory to restore traffic, the simple and crude repairs made difficulties inevitable. Recently, some military personnel who do not understand the truth have frequently interfered, and incidents of assaulting station staff have occurred from time to time. In order to prevent this, the ministry has specifically ordered all responsible supervisors to strictly discipline their subordinates and pay close attention to this matter. In the future, matters related to traffic operations should be absolutely subject to the handling of the responsible personnel of each station section, and no further interference should be made.

Fujian Fuqing County Cracks Down on Counterfeit Taiwan Dollar Printing Organization

[Central News Agency, Fuzhou, 20th] According to a dispatch from Fuqing: The county has recently cracked a case of counterfeiting Taiwan dollars. In the back room of the residence of the main suspect, Wu Changhua, the owner of the counterfeit currency printing workshop, a large bundle of Taiwan dollar paper and several copper molds for banknotes were found in a large vat covered with multiple layers of concealing material. However, the main culprit, Wu, escaped. The case involves many figures behind the scenes, and it is rumored that it is also related to personnel of a certain financial institution in Taiwan. The county government is continuing its investigation.

The verdict was: The defendant committed illegal killings during the war and is sentenced to life imprisonment. Editorial: Establishing a New National Ethos

Since the Legislative Yuan temporarily suspended the review of the draft constitutional amendment due to procedural issues, all parties have paid great attention to the constitutional draft issue. The drafting of the constitutional amendment was originally based on the resolutions of the Political Consultative Conference (PCC). Whether this amendment will be submitted to the National Assembly is not only related to the credibility of the government but also to the future of the overall situation. For this reason, this newspaper has previously commented on the constitutional draft issue, believing that the drafting of a Three Principles of the People constitution has no precedent to follow, and everything is a pioneering effort. The drafting of the May 5th Constitution took great effort and fully reflected the spirit of the Three Principles of the People. However, whether the system it established is the most reasonable in light of the evolution of the past decade, especially in recent years, is also questionable. As for the amended constitutional draft that the government plans to submit to the National Assembly, it still adheres to the solemn stance of the Three Principles of the People while complying with the resolutions of the PCC and should serve as the basis for the National Assembly to formulate the constitution. As for the procedural issues, as long as the Central Standing Committee makes a resolution, it can be made compliant with the regulations in a timely manner.

Now, the Central Standing Committee has indeed passed the constitutional amendment and handed it over to the Legislative Yuan to quickly complete the legislative procedure. At the same time, it also passed the National Government Organization Law Amendment. The Supreme National Defense Council also passed the Executive Yuan Organization Law Amendment. The contents of each proposal all comply with the spirit of the PCC resolutions. The passage of this motion can, on the one hand, enable the Legislative Yuan to review the constitutional amendment in accordance with the legal procedures, complete the review in a timely manner, and submit it to the National Assembly. On the other hand, it shows the people of the country how the government will abide by its promises and resolutely adopt the resolutions passed by the PCC. All absurd talk can be disproved by the Central Standing Committee's resolution this time. The government values its own promises and will not easily allow them to be changed. Unless it is outside of the fundamental stance, the central government's impartiality should indeed move people from all parties and factions, even those without any affiliation. The outdated notion that "only by believing in our doctrine can you be our citizen" may still linger in the minds of some people, but it can never represent a political group that is truly dedicated to serving the public. Only those political groups that outwardly advocate democracy but actually have no individual freedom and worship collectivism have such a terrible notion.

The National Government Organization Law Amendment passed by the Central Standing Committee stipulates that in addition to the Chairman of the National Government being elected by the Central Standing Committee, there will be forty members of the National Government Committee, including people from both within and outside the party, and the power of the National Government Committee will be expanded. At the same time, the Executive Yuan Organization Law Amendment passed by the Supreme National Defense Council stipulates that in addition to changing the Ministry of Transportation to the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Posts and Telecommunications, three new ministries will be established: the Ministry of Land Administration, the Ministry of Water Resources, and the Ministry of Health. There will also be political affairs commissioners. All these resolutions follow the spirit of the PCC resolutions, which shows the government's determination to comply with and implement the PCC resolutions. Due to the passage of this amendment, the reorganization of the National Government and the Executive Yuan to accommodate people from all parties and factions, even those without any affiliation, will be accelerated. We hope that all parties can further cooperate sincerely to make the organization of the National Government and the Executive Yuan more substantial, so as to establish a new model of democratic unity. The future of the nation will thus gain more hope.

Rectifying Border Politics Must Not Be Overlooked

When the domestic situation presents new opportunities due to the convening of the National Assembly, we must not neglect the news and intentions coming from the border regions. A few days ago, the Inner Mongolian representatives to the National Assembly, all Inner Mongolian senators to the Political Participation Council, and other Mongolian and Xinjiang figures gathered in Beijing and issued a declaration demanding autonomy and requesting the central government to thoroughly implement the Second Plenary Session's resolution on border politics and to revitalize border governance. At the same time, according to a United Press report from Los Angeles, the Xinjiang issue seems to be resurfacing, and the old dream of the "East Turkistan People's Republic" is showing signs of revival. The reliability of this report from Los Angeles across the Pacific is questionable. In our judgment, the former report inevitably exaggerates the situation and is not necessarily credible. However, since there is such a report, it is indeed worthy of our vigilance.

The importance of valuing our border politics is beyond our need to emphasize. Xinjiang and Mongolia serve as the northern and northwestern barriers of our country. At this time, it is certainly worthy of our attention. In the past eight years, some parts of Mongolia and Xinjiang were occupied and suffered from the aggression of Japanese warlords. After the surrender of the Japanese invaders, they were subjected to the rule of armed forces other than the National Army and the Chinese Communist Party. Therefore, just as they were celebrating the recovery of their homeland, they suffered from another violent rule. Therefore, we should express our utmost sympathy and consolation to our compatriots in Mongolia and Xinjiang. The central government cared about the border people and dispatched Mongolian Banner Comfort Missions after Japan's surrender last year. Due to the recent developments in the situation, the Mongolia and Xinjiang areas have inevitably suffered from the impact of unrest. According to news from foreign news agencies, one report said that the Outer Mongolian troops are currently concentrating on the border area of Chahar Province; another report said that the Outer Mongolian Military Bureau is currently taking strict measures to prevent anyone from crossing the border from Chahar Province into Outer Mongolia. Although the accuracy of these reports remains to be confirmed, the unrest in the Mongolia border situation seems undeniable.

At this time, we see voices from Mongolian figures demanding autonomy. According to news reports, the Mongolian compatriots' demand for autonomy is not for separation, but for the government to fulfill the promises it has made to the Mongolian people time and time again. We believe that this statement comes from the hearts of our Mongolian Banner compatriots. The Mongolian Banner compatriots face Outer Mongolia across the Gobi Desert and know the actual situation of Outer Mongolia more clearly. Moreover, they also know the violence of the Chinese Communist Party's rule. Therefore, their minds are inward, not for separation. We admire the Mongolian Banner compatriots for being able to express themselves so frankly. The central government's attention to border politics has important resolutions in the Second Plenary Session. One is that under the principle of forming a unified democratic country based on the Three Principles of the People and the May 5th Constitution, the constitution must clearly stipulate guaranteeing the rights and interests of border ethnic groups. The other is that the members of the National Government Committee and the political affairs commissioners of the Executive Yuan after the reorganization must include loyal and capable continuers of the Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui ethnic groups. Furthermore, capable people from the Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui ethnic groups must have ample opportunities to participate in the actual work of various departments and commissions. The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission will be reorganized into the Ministry of Border Affairs, so that capable people from the Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui ethnic groups can participate in actual work and assume actual responsibilities. In the education of all levels in the border ethnic areas, emphasis should be placed on the native language. Reasonable regulations should be made for the autonomous system in the border areas according to the actual situation of each place. Regarding the Inner Mongolia portion, the original Mongolian Local Autonomous Political Affairs Committee will be restored, and the powers and limits of the league banner government and the provincial and county boundaries will be clearly divided. This newspaper has previously commented on these decisions, believing that "the resolutions of this Second Plenary Session of the Kuomintang not only expanded the opportunities for border compatriots to participate in the central government, but also focused on supporting the autonomy of border compatriots and maintaining the inherent cultural life of border compatriots, which not only shows the central government's concern for border compatriots, but also opens up a broad avenue for their future development." Unfortunately, after the Second Plenary Session, the domestic situation still failed to move towards peace, so the aforementioned decisions could not be implemented. Now that the situation has changed, and the Mongolian compatriots have demands for autonomy, we urge the central government to implement the decisions. We uphold the central government's virtuous intention to care for the border people and sympathize with the Mongolian compatriots' experiences. Therefore, we hope that the resolutions of the Second Plenary Session on border politics will be implemented in a timely and gradual manner to satisfy the border people's longing.

As for the Xinjiang portion, the news from the United States is not necessarily credible, as we have said before. However, we cannot help but reiterate here that the central government, based on the Three Principles of the People of the revolution, aims to coordinate the border people and stabilize the frontiers. In January of this year, the eleven-article text of the reconciliation agreement for the Yining dispute was signed, and in June of this year, two additional articles were established. At the same time, the organization of the Xinjiang Provincial Government was expanded, and members from various ethnic groups residing in Xinjiang were appointed as committee members. It can be seen that the central government is doing its best to support the autonomy of the border people and to satisfy all the wishes of the border people that can be satisfied. This enlightened policy should be supported by the border people. Therefore, how to harmonize all ethnic groups, eliminate suspicions, and achieve sincere cooperation should be the focus of the unified efforts of all ethnic groups in Xinjiang. Due to the transmission of the aforementioned reports, we reiterate our views in particular. We hope that the people of the country will encourage each other.

Rushing to Repair the Hai'ning Juezi Embankment; the Brushwood Embankment Project Has Begun; and a New Concrete Embankment Will Be Built on the Original Site

[Our Newspaper, Hangzhou] The Qiantang River Seawall Engineering Bureau recently decided to completely repair the seawall in the next two years, and then begin the fundamental management project of the Qiantang River from 1948 (Republic Year 37), aiming to complete the project within three years, so that the downstream riverbed of the Qian River can be fixed and the disaster of the seawall collapsing will not occur again. The "Juezi" number seawall in Haining was destroyed. The bureau decided to build a new concrete seawall 30 meters long on the original site. Before it is completed, a brushwood embankment will be built first to avoid negligence. The brushwood embankment project has already begun. As for the equipment needed to build the new concrete seawall, the Executive Yuan's Relief and Rehabilitation Administration is shipping it from Shanghai and it can also be put into operation within days. After the completion of this seawall, a 150-meter water barrier will also be added to prevent the river from approaching the base of the seawall and ensure safety. As for the collapse of the Xiaoshan Nan River, the bureau has also drafted a plan for rushing repairs, intending to stop the embankment first to prevent the tide from invading. However, according to past practice, the local people must repair it themselves, and the Seawall Engineering Bureau can only assist from the side.

Suzhou Cloth Factories Request Cotton Yarn Allocation

[Our Newspaper, Suzhou] There are as many as forty-two weaving factories in Suzhou, and the demand for cotton yarn is quite large. However, in the past six months, due to the depletion of cotton yarn stocks, all factories have had to purchase from the black market. The prices are high, the purchases are not easy, and the costs have increased, resulting in sluggish sales of products. Therefore, cloth prices have fallen from time to time, and the factories have suffered huge losses, feeling that they cannot maintain operations. This is an unprecedented crisis for the Suzhou cloth factory industry. Wu Zhenshan, Chairman of the Cloth Factory Industry Association, recently heard that fellow weaving factories in Shanghai have obtained a general allocation of cotton yarn. On the 18th, he urgently telegraphed the county chamber of commerce, requesting that it consider the difficult and precarious situation of all Suzhou cloth factories and promptly forward the request to the Shanghai Textile Industry Management Committee to instruct the Sixth District Cotton Yarn Industry Association to allocate cotton yarn nearby, following the example of fellow cloth factories in Shanghai and Changzhou, in order to maintain production.

崑松 Launches Winter Defense; Cheng-Xi-Wu Joint Defense is in Progress

[Our Jiangyin Dispatch] In recent days, bandit alarms have frequently occurred in various districts of the western countryside. The county government, fearing potential future troubles if vigorous efforts are not made to eliminate them, believes that the best solution is to restore the joint defense mechanism among Cheng, Xi, and Wu counties. Prominent local figures will be selected to oversee the effort to quell banditry. The position of director is proposed to be filled by former Magistrate of Ning County, Xu Bingquan. The matter has been submitted to the Capital Garrison Headquarters for approval. Furthermore, to prevent banditry, Commander Tang has ordered a rapid reorganization of the township and baojia (household registration) system throughout the county. Joint guarantee and collective responsibility pledges will be implemented, and road protection villages will be reliably organized. A flexible and comprehensive communication and intelligence network will be established, and self-defense forces will be strengthened. These measures are to be implemented by the 30th of this month. Starting December 1st, the headquarters will dispatch special commissioners to inspect various counties.

[Our Kunshan Dispatch] To ensure the achievements of the suppression efforts and maintain public security, the county government convened a winter defense conference on the afternoon of the 18th. The following key resolutions were made: (1) Division of defense zones: Urban and rural areas will be divided into separate defense zones, with the military police and security forces jointly responsible for them. (2) Implementation of watch and patrol, and strict enforcement of prohibitions: From 12:00 midnight to 5:00 AM the following morning, all pedestrians and vehicles will be prohibited from passing. (3) Intensification of inspections: The military police will be jointly responsible, and the training of self-defense forces in various townships will be strengthened. A communication system will be established in each township area, and a plan will be formulated and submitted for approval.

[Our Songjiang Dispatch] Due to the repeated occurrence of theft and robbery cases in the past, the police station of our county's urban area has requested to strengthen its defenses and consolidate public security as the winter season approaches. It has been decided that winter defense will commence immediately. Every night, all shops and households must close their doors by 10:00 PM, and public venues must cease operations by 12:00 midnight. From 12:00 midnight to 5:00 AM, there will be a curfew. Only military police in uniform and those with permits will be allowed to pass after being inspected by patrol teams. All other traffic will be prohibited. Boats on the river will also be prohibited from sailing during the same hours. Other measures, such as implementing joint patrols, reporting theft and robbery, and conducting random household checks, have also been agreed upon.

[Our Mingguang Dispatch] Two hundred rifles, previously requested from the Xuzhou Pacification Commissioner's Office and the Anhui Provincial Security Headquarters, have been successively transported to Mingguang by assigned personnel. They will be distributed according to the needs of various townships, and in accordance with the provincial government's Five-Year Plan for Building a New Anhui, a county-wide people's self-defense corps will be organized and trained to strengthen local security forces. To ensure local public security, a winter defense committee has also been established.

Reader's Opinions - Agreement Regulations

(1) This column is absolutely open, and the authors are responsible for their own writing. However, it is important to avoid length. (2) Do not attack private individuals, and do not submit the same article to multiple publications. (3) Contributors must write "Reader's Opinions Manuscript" and provide their real name and address, but they may use a pen name when published. (4) No payment will be made for articles in this column. (5) This newspaper has the right to abridge submitted articles. (6) Whether or not a submitted article is published will not be replied to. (7) This newspaper may, when necessary, forward submitted articles to relevant agencies for reference.

Public Buses Incite Passengers to Curse

The Nanshi district after the war has been washed by artillery fire quite miserably, but at present there are already several places under construction of new houses, and the number of homes and shops has also increased compared to before, so the market is gradually recovering prosperity. For the convenience of citizens' transportation, the municipal authorities have public bus facilities, and the general salaried employees and working-class people are all pleased and find it convenient. However, it has recently been rumored that when these buses come, four or five of them connect one after another, and they drive away quickly without opening the doors when they arrive at the station, leaving passengers who have been waiting for a long time unable to board.

One day last month, the writer happened to finish a meeting at the General Labor Union and felt quite tired. When he arrived at Xiaobeimen, he planned to take Route 6, but waited for about fifteen minutes without seeing a bus coming. Just as he was getting impatient, he saw three or five of them driving up at the same time. When the buses arrived at the station, the first bus drove away without opening its doors because it was already full of passengers. The passengers on the second bus surged to the door before the bus had stopped. The passengers inside the bus were sparser than on the previous bus. The driver and ticket seller shouted, "There are empty buses in the back!" Before they could finish speaking, the bus had already started moving. As a result, the general passengers rushed to the buses in the back. The bus carriages were naturally much emptier than the previous two buses, but the ticket sellers shouted "Empty in the back" in unison, and at the same time, with a blow of the whistle, the three buses chased after them like they were flying away. The general passengers showed disappointment and hatred as they cursed: "Damn it! I can walk myself," "Run, run!" Several people who could not wait any longer cursed and ran away. As the sky gradually darkened, the writer was fortunate enough to be returning home in the evening. Since he had nothing to do, he decided to wait a bit longer, and at the same time, he took the opportunity to watch the skilled little technicians repairing three-wheeled vehicles by the roadside, making it a source of amusement in his boredom. Unconsciously, he waited for another ten minutes, and four buses drove up in a row. The first and second buses were packed with passengers, so they drove away without stopping. The third and fourth buses were relatively empty. The passengers rushed to the doors before the buses had stopped, but as before, the ticket seller pointed to the back and shouted, "Empty buses are coming in the back!" At this time, the maintainer could not help but sigh secretly, and then heard the passengers cursing endlessly, "Chinese people can never do things well!" This sentence made people hear "It's too sad!" Although the writer is just a small civil servant, he absolutely hopes that the people after the victory will still have such a contemptuous evil [attitude] towards state-owned enterprises! Therefore, he raises the following points, hoping that Director Zhao and the responsible personnel in the transportation department will pay attention to and improve them. (1) If the buses arrive at the same time in connection, is it that the ticket sellers have a role in making the ticket inspectors unable to take care of both ends? (2) If there are vacant spots in the bus, why don't you open the door to accommodate passengers when you arrive at the station? (3) Since Laoximen is the starting point, why doesn't the manager of the dispatch dispatch the buses at evenly spaced intervals so that several buses can be dispatched at the same time? (4) In Shanghai, where transportation tools are competing with foreign countries, the drivers and ticket sellers should have the necessary politeness to improve the passengers. If there is no substantial training, there is no superiority or inferiority from those run by foreign merchants, then the leakage of passengers taking the foreign merchants' vehicles every day, over time, cannot be said to be a loss to the country. (5) It is best to appoint a few mobile inspectors to check whether the drivers and ticket sellers are on duty and can give passengers assistance when getting on and off the bus. (6) If any business does not have sufficient remuneration in life, malpractice and disloyal duties are prone to occur, so the treatment of service personnel should also be rationalized, otherwise, even if the above points can be improved, it is only a symptomatic but not a root cause, because work efficiency is embedded in work mood, and service spirit is contained in service interest (Zhang Zhi)

Looking back on the sudden outbreak of the August 13th Shanghai Battle, the Japanese pirates took advantage of the opportunity to land at Jinshanwei Haikou (November 5th of that year), and almost the entire southeastern half fell into the hands of the enemy pirates. Therefore, after painfully reflecting on it, it seems that the collapse of the Jinshanwei coastal defense should be considered the most serious and painful. According to Jinshanwei City, it was built by Qi Jiguang during the Ming Dynasty to defend against Japanese pirates. Unexpectedly, more than 300 years later, [the] same [Japanese] pirates broke through the gate and rushed in. Therefore, in order to alert the people to pay attention to coastal defense and refine the navy, in order to commemorate the major damage suffered during this war of resistance, and in order to mourn the lives and property sacrificed due to the sudden loss of Jinshanwei, it seems that something should be expressed. Perhaps a road should be designated in one of our country's major cities and named Jinshanwei Road (it is most appropriate to rename a street in Shanghai), or a stele should be erected near Jinshanwei City where the Japanese pirates first landed, in order to be vigilant and commemorate, which has profound significance. (Gongdu)

Mail Reply

Reply to Mr. Wang Hucheng: Regarding your letter pointing out that a piece of mail was shelved, the Shanghai Postal Administration replied: "It has been found that a regular letter sent from Yin County to Mr. Wang was indeed delayed. The reason is that at present, both this office and the Yin County office have a large number of mails received and dispatched, which has caused the handling to be slower. We have ordered [them] to improve and have sent a letter to the Yin County office to pay attention. However, the war item was indeed properly delivered on the 13th of last month, but it was not delivered on the day when your housemates lived on the same day, resulting in [being] left for one day. Mr. Wang has issued a letter to prove that the post-delivery time often has been misplaced by the concierge or housemates, and this bureau has repeatedly notified the public to pay attention." Special delivery.

UN General Assembly Passes Resolution to End Religious and Racial Discrimination

Gu Weijun's Elucidation of Confucius' Philosophy Wins Applause from the Audience

[Central News Agency, New York, 19th Dispatch] The UN General Assembly held its first vote today among 54 countries and unanimously passed a resolution proposed by Egypt, requesting all governments to "immediately cease religious and so-called racial persecution and discrimination." The only opponent was South African Prime Minister Smuts, who coldly read the newspaper on the sidelines during the General Assembly's discussion of the resolution, presumably because India would present evidence of racial discrimination against South Africa.

[French News Agency, New York, 19th Dispatch] The United Nations General Assembly met today to discuss Egypt's proposal on racial and religious discrimination. Egyptian representative Audian first spoke, saying that Egypt's proposal could be seen as a "symbol of good triumphing over evil." The Polish representative expressed direct endorsement and said that Poland has suffered greatly from racial discrimination. Soviet representative Vyshinsky also strongly supported the proposal, but said that the proposal was too abstract and could not point out practical ways to oppose exclusion. At this point, Chinese

Dr. Wellington Koo stood up and said that the proposal put forward by the Egyptian representative was fully in line with the United Nations Charter, and the Chinese delegation fully expressed its approval. Although this proposal does not have any specific provisions, there are still many countries that have not respected the concept of human equality, so the Chinese representative expressed unlimited welcome to Egypt's proposal. As for China, it had already respected the principle of human equality 5,000 years ago, and to this day, it has also implemented these principles. There are five different ethnic groups in China, Han, Manchu, Mongolian, Hui, and Tibetan, whose beliefs can represent all the religions in the world, but they can still coexist peacefully and live in harmony, which is why China can implement the principle of human equality. China's first teacher, Confucius, said, "All within the four seas are brothers." We always keep Confucius' teachings in mind and earnestly follow them. We deeply hope that the General Assembly will unanimously pass the proposal put forward by Egypt. Soviet representative Vyshinsky expressed that although the Soviet Union will vote for the proposal, it felt that the failure of the proposal to list factual country names and the lack of specific measures to prevent discrimination were shortcomings. US representative Austin and British representative Shawcross also spoke successively in support of the resolution. [Shawcross] also expressed support for Vyshinsky's meaning, pointing out that words and resolutions alone are still not enough, so the United Kingdom always strives to complete the Human Rights Commission in the Taijie Conference to stipulate the code of basic human rights. The Indian representative said that this proposal is a major step in determining the complete equality of human beings, regardless of whether they are white, black, or yellow. He deeply hoped that this proposal would be unanimously passed and that the representatives of all countries would study the situation in their own countries after returning home and try to find ways to remedy any existing discrimination. Finally, French representative Barodie spoke and said that the French representative expressed support for this proposal, but I want to tell you that France has never allowed any racial discrimination. Such discrimination is absolutely inconsistent with the spirit of the French people.

Security Council Re-elects Members; Colombia, Syria, and Belgium Elected; Social and Economic Council Members US and Lebanon Reelected

[United States News Agency, New York, 19th Dispatch] The United Nations General Assembly elected Colombia, Syria, and Belgium today as non-permanent members of the Security Council for a term of two years. The "UNGA" plenary session also elected Venezuela and New Zealand as members of the Social and Economic Council for a term of three years. The United States and Lebanon were also re-elected to continue their terms. The Social and Economic Council still lacks two seats, but because the voting results were not enough two-thirds, the four candidates (Turkey, Netherlands, Belarus, and Yugoslavia) were not elected. General Assembly Chairman Spaak then announced that it would be decided at the next plenary session. Due to today's election results, the Security Council's eleven members next year will be: the five permanent members (US, UK, China, Soviet Union, France), as well as Australia, Brazil, and Poland (the term of the above three countries will expire at the end of 1947), and Colombia, Syria, and Belgium elected today. Next year, the members of the Economic and Social Council will be: Cuba, Czechoslovakia, India, Norway, the Soviet Union, the United Kingdom (the term will expire at the end of 1947), Belgium, Canada, Chile, China, France, Secret (the term will expire at the end of 1948), and the four countries elected today (the United States, Venezuela, Lebanon, and New Zealand) and the two countries not yet elected, whose terms will all end at the end of 1949.

Anglo-German Issue: Six Guiding Principles Determined

[Agence France-Presse, London, 19th] Well-informed sources here recently stated that the United States, Britain, France, and the Soviet Union will soon hold a meeting in New York to discuss the German problem. The position that Britain should defend at that time has been clearly defined. Foreign Secretary Bevin is reported to have prepared a memorandum outlining Britain's arguments. In essence, there are the following six points: (1) Britain advocates that Germany should be unified politically and economically under a system that is neither centralized nor federal. (2) Britain believes that Germany's production, as stipulated in the Potsdam Agreement, is insufficient. Therefore, Germany should be allowed to produce 11 million tons of steel annually, with the proceeds used to purchase food. (3) Under the current reparations plan, Britain objects to any removal of equipment from Germany by either the Soviet Union or Western countries, even if the Soviet Union proposes installment deductions. Britain will only abandon this view when Germany's production increases sufficiently to cover the costs of Allied occupation and supplies. (4) Britain would prefer to merge the British and American occupation zones rather than enter into an agreement allowing the Soviet Union to remove equipment from Germany as reparations during the period when Germany relies on British supplementation. (5) Britain is still willing to invite the Soviet Union to participate in the control of the Ruhr region's industry within a unified German organization. (6) Britain intends to propose the organization of a central German institution, the establishment of a central civil service corps, and the appointment of local government agencies with the power to make decisions politically, but ultimately subject to the approval of the occupying powers.

US Drafts Disarmament Plan

[United Press, New York, 19th] US officials are currently drafting a disarmament proposal, which they believe will lead the world towards disarmament and ensure the security of the United States. It is expected that the proposal will be formally submitted to the UN General Assembly at the end of this week or early next week. Authoritative sources say that the draft will require the following points as the price for countries to participate: (1) Effective guarantees that no country will undermine the established goals of disarmament. (2) Guarantees that other countries will implement disarmament to the same extent as the United States and fully fulfill their promises. This plan is the US response to Molotov's disarmament proposals in the UN organization. The plan will be submitted to President Truman for approval before it is released.

Draft Approved by the General Assembly

Guo stated that the Chinese government will sign the draft agreement as soon as possible. Also, the General Assembly today unanimously passed the draft, but it will only take effect after it has been signed by more than 35 countries.

US Coal Miners' Strike Has Significant Impact at Home and Abroad

[United Press, Pittsburgh, 19th] Although the federal court ordered a ban on the bituminous coal miners' strike, the number of strikers continues to increase. Yesterday, 38,000 miners were on strike, and today another 40,000 are on strike, totaling about 78,000. Two hundred and seventy-two coal mines are closed, resulting in a daily reduction of 20% in coal production. Fuel supplies to steel mills have begun to be disrupted, and some mines in those plants are also on strike. Whether a nationwide coal strike will begin will be known on the 21st. Lewis, the former chairman of the Mine Workers Union, has notified the government that the union contract expires on that date. Since the strike ban was issued, Lewis has not made any statement.

[United Press, Washington, 19th] The War Department announced today that it is prepared to join forces with the Interior Department to intervene in the coal miners' strike, but has not yet received a notice to deploy troops.

[Reuters, Washington, 19th] Acting Secretary of State Acheson told reporters today that the impending national coal miners' strike is a major blow to countries that need US food and coal. If all 400,000 bituminous coal miners in the country go on strike, the export of coal and food will inevitably stop.

[United Press, Washington, 19th] Secretary of the Interior Krug predicted today that the coal miners' strike would have a huge impact on all aspects of national life. It is said that within 60 days of the strike, it could shut down 64% of publicly owned utilities powered by electricity, 60% of steel mills, 90% of coking plants, 86% of first-class railway companies, 90% of cement plants, and 70% of other factories.

[United Press, Tokyo, 20th] According to reliable sources today, the US prosecutor at the Far East Tribunal originally hoped to conclude the presentation of evidence related to the 27 Japanese war criminals in early December, but because the British and Philippine prosecutors insisted on presenting all documents of Japanese atrocities, it is feared that it will not be possible to end it as scheduled. Prosecutors from the eleven countries have recently held repeated meetings and attached great importance to the conspiracy charges in the indictment. The indictment accuses the defendants of "planning, instigating, and engaging in a war of aggression." After US Navy Admiral Lee Richardson submits a detailed report on the attack on Pearl Harbor next week, this stage of the indictment can actually be concluded. The US prosecutor believes that only by briefly presenting special examples of Japanese military atrocities can the presentation of the entire case be completed in the second week of December.

Social Phenomenon Under High Pressure Living

Japanese University Students Compete to Be Western Musicians

[Kaizosha, Tokyo, 19th] Amid the postwar wave of inflation, the number of Japanese students seeking jobs to pay tuition and maintain their living expenses is increasing day by day. Those with skills do not have to worry about finding a way out. Currently, there are as many as 17 orchestras in Tokyo dance halls composed of university students, each earning between 16,000 and 20,000 yuan per month, which is quite enviable for civil servants and teachers whose monthly salaries are less than 1,000 yuan. According to Ohashi, a student in the music department of Keio University, since April of this year, the number of students organizing orchestras has gradually increased. He works at the Shirokiya dance hall from 1:00 to 4:30 every day, and at the Yaen dance hall from 5:30 to 9:00 in the afternoon, earning more than 20,000 yuan in busy months. However, it is still difficult to decide whether to completely abandon their studies and make this a career, or to continue their studies and make this a side job. Seriously considering the future is quite worrying.

Woman Appointed Chair of Parliament: A First in Britain

[Reuters, London, 19th] Labour MP Mrs. Barton was elected today as one of the twelve chairpersons of the current session of the House of Commons. It is unprecedented in Britain for a woman to serve as chair of parliament. When the parliament holds meetings of the standing committees, Mrs. Barton will serve as chair. However, when the parliament discusses budget issues, the parliament will become a committee, and Mrs. Barton will serve as chair of the entire House of Commons meeting. The chairperson must be familiar with procedural law and know the names of all members of the House of Commons. Mrs. Barton's husband, Mr. Barton, is also a member of the House of Commons, and the two often sit together during meetings.

China in the Eyes of the British

—Sent by Zhu Zunxu, Our Newspaper's Correspondent in the United Kingdom

Although the news from China is unfavorable, the British public's opinion of China is not bad. The London Times publishes news about China every day, and publishes an editorial on China every month or two. Every year on Double Ten Day, the Times publishes an article analyzing the Chinese situation. The Times's position is fair, and it often criticizes the CCP's illegal and reckless behavior. Other London newspapers rarely publish Chinese news. Occasionally, they publish one or two articles, but 19 out of 20 are in the style of tabloids or evening newspapers. For example, what Chinese people eat, what they wear, and photos of young ladies wearing qipaos often appear in the gossip columns or miscellaneous sections of various newspapers. The News Chronicle used to publish many articles about China because of Geld, who promoted the CCP. However, he himself did not sympathize with the CCP. In fact, it was because he had disagreements with several spokespersons in Chongqing, and as a result, he developed a dislike for the entire Chinese government. When his dislike reached its extreme, he actually sided with the CCP. The Chronicle's view of China has gradually been corrected. Their political commentator, Mr. Bartley, is about to visit China. Mr. Bartley's world political vision has always been admired by the British. His view of the September 18th Incident is completely consistent with China's view. The Manchester Guardian, which has always been considered by the Chinese to sympathize with China, publishes very little news about China. Occasionally, there is an editorial, but its tone does not show "sympathy."

British magazines have mixed effects on China. The "Economist," the most influential weekly magazine, often has articles on China. Regarding China's inflation, it bluntly pointed out that the civil war is the root of all evils. This time, the leftist weekly magazine "New Statesman and Nation" has a tone about China that is somewhat similar to "Xinhua" and "Liberation." Its position is well known, just like the Daily Worker (organ of the British Communist Party), whose views are not taken seriously. The most successful point of the CCP's external propaganda is their so-called "peasant movement," which boasts of its rent reduction and other land reform policies in the border areas. Most British newspapers, including The Times, believe that the CCP has a solution to this urgent social problem.

The British are generally not concerned about the Hong Kong issue. Some people are very willing to return this island to China. Those who oppose it are still the "old China hands." What the people in Britain understand the least is: why do the Chinese in Hong Kong have such a deep dislike for the British? This suspicion is very natural, because the British in England do not know the life attitudes of the British in colonies, semi-colonies, and quasi-colonies - the arrogance of imperialists. These imperialists swagger and dominate abroad, but when they return home, their attitude changes and they are the same as ordinary, humorous British people.

The British do not understand China enough. Our country's foreign propaganda authorities should pay attention, but relying on propaganda alone is not enough. To make a nation understand us, introducing cultural life is one way; but clarifying the current domestic situation is the first thing. Everyone knows that China has a long history and a great culture, but if what is revealed from this great cultural background is all bad news, the big question mark in foreigners' minds will never be eliminated. (End)

Although the "Rebellious Party" Trend in Britain Has Subsided, the Political Situation is Still Not Optimistic; The Opposition Accounts for More Than One-Third of the House; The Internal Split of the Labour Party Remains the Same

[United Press, London, 19th] Although the House of Commons voted 335 to 0 last night to express confidence in the government's current foreign policy, 160 Labour MPs did not vote. Except for those who were ill or had other reasons, at least 100 Labour MPs made no indication when voting. The high proportion is worrying even if the government claims victory. Among the members who participated in the vote, there were 230 Labour members, 104 Conservative members, 7 Liberal members, and 12 members from various small parties. According to those who support the government, the vote of confidence is enough to show the world that British public opinion supports Foreign Secretary Bevin. However, critics say that the large number of abstaining members proves that the Labour Party's policy is still split in reality and has not been remedied as a result. There is a possibility that rebellious actions will occur again. The government should not ignore this crisis and say that everything is calm. The rebellious members explained the reasons for their abstention, saying that this vote cannot be interpreted as a general distrust of the government. For example, they fully agree with the government's domestic policies, and even have no objection to certain parts of its foreign policy. Therefore, the government's obtaining a majority of confidence in the House of Commons is due to the following two reasons: (1) In terms of domestic affairs, the Labour Party seems to be as united as ever; (2) In terms of foreign policy, the Conservative Party and loyal members of the Labour Party unanimously support the government.

Beijing-Shanghai Facsimile Telegraph Opens; Sending and Receiving Pictures and Photos Are Flawless; Rates Are Divided into 50,000 Yuan and 20,000 Yuan

[Our Newspaper Report] The Beijing-Shanghai facsimile telegraph service officially opened yesterday. The transmission of text, pictures, and photos is extremely clear. The facsimile telegraph machine at the Shanghai Telecommunications Bureau was installed and tested long ago. The Nanjing side also completed the testing yesterday. After the opening yesterday, Minister Yu of the Ministry of Communications sent a facsimile telegram to Mayor Wu, which read: "To Mayor Wu Guozhen of Shanghai, Honorable Brother: The Ministry is exerting all its efforts to improve the work of various transportation departments. Regarding telecommunications innovation, long-distance telephones have adopted ultra-shortwave wireless machines, and telegraphs have been tested with teletype machines, and special express telegrams have been opened to strive for rapid and accurate communication. Now, facsimile telegraphs are being tested in Beijing and Shanghai. On the occasion of the opening, I respectfully express my feelings and hope for your understanding. Your brother, Yu Dawei, November 20th."

Mayor Wu replied to Minister Yu: "To Minister Yu Dawei of the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing, Honorable Brother: I have received your telegram and learned that since you took over as Minister of Communications, you have been thinking hard and doing your best to improve the transportation industry, adopting new-style machines and testing facsimile telegraphs, so that public and private affairs can be reached in an instant, making the whole country one family and connecting east and west as one place. Promoting it to various places can be expected in the near future. I am deeply impressed and congratulate you. I respectfully reply. Your brother, Wu Guozhen, 20th Secret"

The receiving and sending location for facsimile telegraphs in this city is at the General Business Office of the Shanghai Telecommunications Bureau, No. 70 Fuzhou Road. Before sending, you must first request special paper from that office, which is divided into two types: A and B. Type A costs 50,000 yuan per copy, and Type B costs 20,000 yuan.

Visit and Testing

[Our Newspaper Nanjing, 20th] After several months of efforts by telecommunications personnel in Beijing and Shanghai, the Beijing-Shanghai wireless facsimile has been successfully tested and officially opened. This morning, the reporter visited the receiving station of the Nanjing Telecommunications Bureau, and Director Lei Dahua personally tested the Beijing-Shanghai telefacsimile and added explanations. First, a form was sent from Shanghai to Beijing, and the lines and handwriting were very clear. Nanjing also sent written documents to Shanghai. Paper that is 12 inches wide and 8 inches high can be transmitted in 8 minutes. According to him, because some parts have not yet been installed, the transmission of photos may not be very clear, but the transmission of other originals, regardless of whether they are written in steel pen or ink brush, or even blueprints, can be recognized word by word. If the situation is good, even lead characters of size 5 can be transmitted one by one, and the test results are shown, and some are not much different from ordinary printed matter.

The telefacsimile machines currently used by the Beijing and Shanghai Telecommunications Bureaus were produced by the American Western Union Company in 1942. A total of four machines were shipped to China, two of which are now in Nanjing and two in Shanghai. Soon, one will be shipped to Beiping. This type of machine is newer than the one currently used in Yu Kun, and can send and receive simultaneously, and has automatic equipment, unlike the former, which is troublesome and inconvenient. The order period was very early. Due to the war, it was stored in India for a long time. It was recently transferred from Chongqing to Beijing. Due to repeated relocation and the fact that each machine weighs three tons, it was damaged a lot when it was transported to Beijing, and it needed to be repaired, so the reason why it was delayed to open is because of this.
