Fire at Sea off Sheshan Island at Midnight; Hai Tian Vessel Almost Suffered Disaster; Careless Cargo Escort Caused Combustion of Straw Material on Board; After Rescue by Ship, Vessel Resumed Course to Qinhuangdao Yesterday Morning

The Hai Tian, a giant Liberty ship operated by the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company on the Shanghai-Qinhuangdao route, set sail from Shanghai at about 12 o'clock on the night of the 19th. When it arrived at the waters off Sheshan Island outside the Wusongkou, it suddenly caught fire. The customs patrol boat heard the alarm and rushed to the rescue, and the fire was extinguished. The deck suffered slight damage. The vessel sailed to Qinhuangdao yesterday morning. Afterwards, a reporter from the Huadong News Agency obtained the truth from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company as follows: The company received a fire report from the Hai Tian Vessel by radio the night before and immediately sent personnel to investigate. The cause of the fire was that the straw material that was easy to catch fire was loaded in the cargo, and the cargo escort was careless, causing the straw material to burn. Fortunately, the crew and customs patrol boat officers tried their best to rescue the ship and extinguish the fire. However, two cargo escorts were burned and were brought to Shanghai by the company by rescue ship yesterday morning and sent to the hospital for treatment. They are not in life-threatening danger. It is also learned that the Hai Tian Vessel is the company's largest Liberty ship, with a deadweight tonnage of more than 10,000 tons. This time, it was going to Qinhuangdao to load coal and bring it to Shanghai.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Landing Craft Run Aground Near Wanxian; Cargo Damaged by Moisture; Crew and Passengers Unharmed; French Ship Songdan Has Not Yet Sailed Out

[Our Newspaper Report] The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Chinese-character Hua-character landing craft are all sent to Shanghai and Chongqing because these landing craft have shallow draft and fast speed, so it is suitable to sail on the long Yangtze River. It is learned that the Hua-210 landing craft loaded goods from Chongqing on the 13th of this month and went downstream. At about 9 am the next morning, it ran aground on a reef near Shipo Sai near Wanjiang. The head cabin was pierced and the Yangtze River flooded in. The cargo was damaged by moisture, but fortunately the crew and passengers were unharmed. The craft immediately sent a telegram for help. The Yichang branch received the telegram and immediately sent a barge to the rescue. After receiving the report, the head office also sent the Hua-208 landing craft to tow it. According to the report from the craft, the river water has gradually receded in recent days. Yesterday, the head of the 210 craft was only a foot away from the water surface, and the back was slightly more than two feet away. Although the rice and other goods were taken out, the hull touched the reef and still could not float, so it was impossible to tow it for a while. Rescue efforts are continuing.

The French vessel Songdan, which came to Shanghai for the first time after the war, arrived in port on the 29th of last month. It was originally scheduled to leave Shanghai and return to France on the 14th of this month. Because it was slightly repaired in Shanghai, it was rescheduled to set sail on the 16th. However, the crew suddenly made demands, which prevented it from leaving. Up until the 18th, it had not been resolved. The company telegraphed the Paris head office for instructions. No reply has been received yet, so the return date of the vessel is still not certain. As for passengers, in addition to French residents returning to France, some were Hong Kong passengers, who have already refunded their tickets and taken other vessels. The company's regular postal vessel André Le Bon set off from Marseille on the 15th of last month and is expected to arrive in Shanghai by the end of this month.

Disputes over the Hartung Estate: Nationality Issue to Become the Focus of Contention; Management Insists Hartung Was British; Twelve Iraqi Relatives Decide to Sue

[Report from this newspaper] Regarding the Hartung estate, twelve close relatives from Iraq have recently sent representatives to Shanghai to relitigate the distribution of the estate. Details were reported in this newspaper on the 11th. According to the Hartung Estate Management Office, although Hartung was originally from Iraq, his naturalization as a British citizen is a well-known fact. The British Consulate in Shanghai issued him a passport at the time, which serves as strong evidence. However, the twelve close relatives insist that Hartung did not obtain British citizenship through legal procedures and can also provide evidence. Therefore, Hartung's nationality will be the focus of contention between the two parties in the estate case. The twelve are now considering the amount of the litigation target. Based on current estimates, the Hartung estate is worth over 50 billion legal currency. If this amount is used as the litigation target, the court fees will be as high as 650 million yuan. The majority of Hartung's estate consists of real estate, including over thirty properties, covering a total area of over 400 mu, as well as the Ci Shu and Hartung Buildings. Currently, the income from the real estate is far less than before. The total monthly income from Hartung's real estate is only over 40 million yuan. George Hartung, Luo Youlan, and over ten others each receive just over two million yuan per month. Therefore, it is widely believed that it is unwise for the twelve Iraqis to spend a large amount on litigation fees for a lawsuit with no certainty of success. However, the twelve Iraqis believe that their rights are at stake and must be fought for, and they have sufficient legal basis. They will file a lawsuit with the local court in the coming days.

Winter Relief Fundraising Committee: Fundraising Goal of 600 Million Yuan

Suspicion of Abetting in the Zang Case: Lai Lingnai Indicted by the District Attorney's Office

[Report from this newspaper] Lai Lingnai, a Spanish sailor suspected of abetting in the tragic death of Zang Daer's son, has been investigated by the District Attorney's Office, which has concluded its investigation and filed a public prosecution in accordance with the law. The indictment is as follows: "Lai Lingnai, on September 22nd of this year, at around 10:00 PM, took a rickshaw from the Seamen's Club to the Huadu Dance Hall on Zhongzheng East Road. After getting out of the rickshaw and entering the dance hall, he failed to pay the fare. Zang Daer's son, the rickshaw puller, waited for ten minutes and saw him leave the dance hall and head east. He went forward to collect the fare. Lai Lingnai brushed him off. Zang Daer's son grabbed his arm, and other rickshaw pullers nearby also shouted for the money. Lai Lingnai, seeing this situation, suspected he was about to be beaten. Coincidentally, an American sailor passed by and he called for his help. The sailor, without asking what was happening, punched Zang Daer's son violently. Zang Daer's son fell to the ground, hitting his head and suffering a concussion, which led to his death. Zang Daer's son died from a concussion caused by injuries sustained during his lifetime, as confirmed by the prosecutor and forensic doctor who conducted the examination and filed a report. The defendant, Lai Lingnai, also admitted that he had a dispute over the fare and that the American sailor had punched the rickshaw puller Zang Daer's son, causing him to fall to the ground; however, he denied abetting the act. However, according to the rickshaw pullers Ren Xiaozhu and Liao Yuanshou, who were present at the scene, they both saw the defendant Lai Lingnai say a few words to the sailor before he punched the rickshaw puller. However, they did not understand his words. Considering the circumstances, the defendant Lai Lingnai is suspected of abetting another person in causing injury resulting in death, which violates Article 277, Paragraph 2, Section 1 and Article 219 of the Criminal Law. A public prosecution is filed in accordance with Article 230, Paragraph 1 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. Prosecutor Ji Su."

Agreement Reached on Plasma Issue: US Side Willing to Repay in Kind; Mayor Convened Discussions with All Parties in Harmonious Atmosphere; President Song Declared Government Had No Knowledge

[Report from this newspaper] Regarding the issue of the recall of American plasma, a reasonable solution was reached yesterday afternoon after Mayor Wu convened relevant parties for consultation. The meeting began at 2:30 PM, attended by representatives from the US War Assets Administration, Lida International Trading Company, the US Consulate General, and the US Navy. The consultation proceeded in a harmonious atmosphere. The mayor guaranteed that all plasma inventory could be returned in full. At the same time, the US side was very satisfied with the cooperation of the purchasing merchant and the Chinese government, and immediately expressed its willingness to repay the price in kind, so that the merchant would not suffer a loss. Both sides immediately agreed to this principle. As for which items would be exchanged, it would be decided by the US side after consulting with the Chinese side.

After the agreement was reached, Mayor Wu immediately held a press conference, reading a statement in English from President Song of the Executive Yuan regarding the matter, which stated: "Regarding the discovery of plasma among the large quantity of medical supplies sold by the US War Assets Administration to a Chinese trading company, the Chinese government had no knowledge of this matter until the news was revealed in the newspapers. The purchase by the Chinese merchant was completely legal; however, the government cannot allow the plasma donated by the American people to the Red Cross to be sold. I instructed Mayor Wu yesterday to seal up the plasma inventory and to facilitate an agreement between the US War Assets Administration and the purchasing trading company, so that a reasonable solution can be reached in accordance with normal procedures. I am now pleased to announce that the relevant parties have reached an agreement, and the buyer has agreed to return the plasma to the US Consulate General today through the Municipal Government. I hereby solemnly declare again: This case has nothing to do with the surplus materials on the Pacific Islands purchased by the Chinese government from the United States in August. No Chinese government agency participated in this matter."

Consul General Zhang in New York: Issued Statement in the United States

[Another Report] The matter of the resale of American plasma in Shanghai is currently spreading widely in the United States. The Chinese government is concerned that inaccurate reports may cause misunderstandings and has instructed Zhang Pingqun, the Consul General in New York, to issue a statement on the 19th, stating that the plasma was sold directly by the US Navy through the War Assets Administration to Lida Trading Company, which then resold it to retailers, and has absolutely no connection with the Chinese government.

It is reported that in September, the Shanghai Power Company supplied 18.37 million kilowatt-hours of electricity to textile mills. Zhabei Water and Electricity Company: Preparing to Be Self-Sufficient

[Report from this newspaper] According to Deputy Director Zhang of the Bureau of Public Utilities, the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company has borrowed 2.4 billion yuan from the Shanghai Branch of the Water and Electricity General Administration to repair the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company's water plant, power plant, and generators. The loan will be repaid in installments after one year. The Zhabei Water and Electricity Company suffered significant damage during the war. It is currently repairing and using a 3,200-kilowatt generator. Therefore, most of Zhabei's electricity depends on the Shanghai Water and Electricity Company. The loan will mainly be used for the repair of existing generators and the purchase of new machines, so that Zhabei's water and electricity supply will be self-sufficient.

Three Drug Traffickers Arrested: Opium Hidden in Coal Briquettes

They saw boatmen Wu Xiaohong, Zheng Qingfang (female), and Wu Binggen whispering to each other. When they suddenly saw the police officers arrive, they appeared flustered. They were all detained. Shi found a two-tael piece of opium in a pile of coal briquettes, eight taels of opium ash in an infant's cradle, and twenty opium bubbles and 110,000 yuan in cash in a bedroom cigarette case. The three and Wu Xiaohong's mother, Wu Fengjin (71 years old), were taken to the station for interrogation. Opium Hidden in Bread and Canned Food: Traffickers from Tianjin Arrested in Shanghai

[Report from this newspaper] Zhao, the chief of the Lujiiawan Branch, received a tip on the 15th that someone on the Zhixin ship from Tianjin was carrying a large quantity of opium. He ordered Hao Jingyi, the chief of the criminal section, to investigate. It was learned that a suspect was staying at Room 237, Yuanyuan Hotel, Jiujiang Road. Informants were sent to contact the suspect, pretending to be buyers and asking for a sample. At around 6:00 PM on the 19th, the suspect was lured to the intersection of Chongqing South Road and Changle Road. Hao, along with Patrol Officer Qin Boliang, Sergeant Ma Shaosong, and Li Zhihua, who were disguised and lying in ambush nearby, arrested the suspect when he arrived with a can of pineapple. The suspect confessed that his name was Zhang Douchun, 30 years old, from Tianjin, residing at No. 16, Laoyemiao, Henan, Tianjin. He had brought 60 taels of opium from Tianjin to Shanghai. 30 taels were in the can, and the other 30 taels were hidden in three large Russian bread loaves, each containing about 10 taels. It was high-grade opium from Laobeikou, worth 13 million yuan. He had taken the Zhixin ship from Tianjin on the 11th and arrived on the 16th. He first stayed at the Nanjing Hotel overnight and then moved to Room 237, Yuanyuan Hotel, Jiujiang Road. Six people, including Shi Pengyu, came with him. They came to Shanghai to sell cabbage and had nothing to do with the opium. The opium belonged to him alone. Subsequently, the original case handler went to the room at the Yuanyuan Hotel and found three loaves of opium-filled bread in a box under the bed. They were taken to the station and filed. The branch plans to invite the Health Bureau to inspect the quantity this morning, seal the opium with the Health Bureau, and hand over the suspects to the judicial authorities for investigation.

Fifteen Film and Drama Personalities to be Interrogated by High Court Today; Two Suspicious Films Reviewed Yesterday; Written Opinions Submitted on the Spot; Authorities Hope Those Reported Will Respect the Judiciary and Report When Summoned

[Our Newspaper's Report] The Procuratorate of the High Court of this city will continue its hearing this morning at 9 a.m. to investigate film and drama personalities suspected of collaborating with the enemy. This second batch of those summoned includes Li Huan, Chen Yunshang, Chen Yanyan, Mei Xi, Liu Zhonghao, Zhang Shichuan, Xu Xinfu, Zhou Shimu, Bian Ying, Shi Tingpan, Hu Jinkang, Jin Longzhang, Zhang Xiaohuan, Zhong Baoxuan, and Wu Zhongshan, a total of fifteen individuals. However, due to the failure to deliver some summons, it is feared that many may not be able to appear in court.

[Our Newspaper's Report] During the occupation of this city, many personnel in the film and drama circles remained in Shanghai to work. After the victory, discussions regarding the issue of reporting film personnel who collaborated with the enemy were quite heated, but no results were seen. Until recently, a certain organization suddenly compiled a list of several dozen names and submitted it to the Procuratorate of the High Court for reporting. Currently, the Procuratorate is summoning and investigating them in batches. This move has made film personnel who remained in Shanghai in the past live in constant anxiety. The impact of this has almost brought the nascent film industry to a standstill. In order to clarify right and wrong, and to avoid wrongly accusing or letting off anyone, the Municipal Party Headquarters, in conjunction with relevant organizations and groups, screened two suspicious films, "Spring River's Lasting Regret" and "Ge Shi's Eternal Fame," at the Shanghai Guangda Theater yesterday morning for review. Those present included Fang Zhi, Xie Renzhao, Sun Dongcheng, and Xu Mingya from the Municipal Party Headquarters; Wang Guanqing from the Municipal Government; Luo Xuelian from the Central Propaganda Department; Li Ximou and Peng Zhenqiu from the Education Bureau; Chen Shenxiu and Xia Jingtao from the Social Affairs Bureau; Du Tongsun and Jiang Bin from the Film Censorship Office; Wu Huasheng from the Youth League; Liu Deming from the Friends of the Military Society; Zhu Renyi from China Electric; Liang Gengshun and Yang Shounian from the District Procuratorate; Zhang Che from the Shanghai Municipal Cultural Movement Committee; and thirty to forty reporters from various newspapers. Qu Rong, the prosecutor from the High Court Procuratorate in charge of investigating film and drama personnel who collaborated with the enemy, also attended with his clerk. "Spring River's Lasting Regret" was screened first at 9 a.m., followed by a ten-minute break, and then "Ge Shi's Eternal Fame" was screened. It was already 1:30 p.m. when the screening was completed. Each participant in the review received a feedback form. The opinions on the two films, collected anonymously, were sealed on the spot and sent to the High Court Procuratorate as a reference for the investigation.

Reflections After Viewing

Chairman Fang of the Municipal Party Headquarters stated after the viewing: "Ge Shi's Eternal Fame" was filmed before "Spring River's Lasting Regret." This is a historical film, and under the military rule of the Japanese at the time, being able to say 'Chinese people will not be slaves to a conquered nation' was truly remarkable. The Japanese were probably not satisfied with 'Ge Shi's Eternal Fame,' hence the existence of 'Spring River's Lasting Regret.' Moreover, the Japanese participated in it. What is noteworthy in that film is that when subtitles appeared, the Japanese were always listed first, followed by the Chinese. And the drama quietly arose from fabrication. As far as I know, the Japanese sonnō jōi movement has no connection with the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom." Secretary-General Xie Renzhao of the Municipal Party Headquarters also said: "'Ge Shi's Eternal Fame' narrates Lin Zexu's ban on opium and resistance against the British. At that time, British imperialism certainly acted in this way, and there were indeed organizations such as the 'Anti-British Corps' in various places. Therefore, this film should be considered from two perspectives: first, in terms of narrating history, there is nothing to criticize; second, in terms of current international relations, since we are currently allies with Great Britain, it seems to present a problem. Regarding the conclusion of 'Spring River's Lasting Regret' that the Japanese sympathized with the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, there seems to be no such record in history. The Japanese emphasized this to make the Chinese people feel favorable towards them."

Before the participants filled out their review opinions, Chairman Fang stated: "I hope everyone will criticize from an objective standpoint and that those who have been reported will report to the court according to the summons and respect the judiciary."

Jiang Shangpei and Others Declared Not Guilty; Xie Guangming Sentenced to Two and a Half Years

[Our Newspaper's Report] The High Court yesterday announced the verdicts in two cases of suspected traitors: (1) Jiang Shangpei, former head of the Judicial Section of the New City Police Branch of the Puppet Shanghai Municipal Government, Xie Guangming, deputy detective, Li Yongde, and Xu Shu, detective leader, were accused of illegally detaining people by abusing their power and infringing on their personal freedom. Jiang, now the head of the Judicial Section of the Old City Gate Branch of this city, denied illegally detaining merchants during the trial, stating that the reason he continued to serve in the puppet police station was to participate in intelligence work for the Sanmin Zhuyi Youth League, which was testified to by Yang Wenguang of the Fourth Division of the Shanghai Branch. He also participated in the anti-enemy police affairs led by Gan Jingxian, which can be proven by letters from Wu Tiecheng and Yu Hongjun to Qian Dajun. Wei Zhongda, who is currently employed by the Garrison Command, was also rescued from danger and provided with travel expenses by Jiang when he was harmed in the past, which was also testified to by Feng. Yesterday, Jiang, Li, and Xu were all declared not guilty. Xie Guangming was sentenced to two and a half years.

Gas, Ferry, and Small Train Prices Will be Adjusted Soon Zhao Zengjue Reported at the Municipal Council Yesterday

Zhao Zengjue, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, reported on the process of adjusting public utility prices at the Public Utilities Committee of the Municipal Council yesterday afternoon. He stated that the Public Utilities Bureau believes that public utility companies should be given reasonable profits and that their profits should be protected; otherwise, no one would be willing to invest in public utilities. This adjustment will not be made for those who can maintain their operations. For example, the Shanghai Telephone Company originally charged based on the number of calls, and the current increase in the number of calls has exceeded expectations, resulting in increased revenue and preventing losses. Therefore, no adjustment was made at all. For those who cannot maintain their operations, reasonable adjustments will be made based on their income and expenses. So far, those that have been approved include electricity, tap water, trams, and buses. Those under consideration include gas, ferries, the "Jidu," Shangnan, and Shangchuan small trains, which will be announced soon. This time, the bureau approved the prices of various companies, both to provide reasonable profits and to encourage them to increase capital and expand equipment to meet the needs of the people. For example, each power company was ordered to increase power generation, and the British and French tram companies were ordered to increase vehicles and handle the track connection from Jing'an Temple to Xujiahui Road. This week, the Public Transportation Company Preparatory Office was also ordered to increase the number of buses and pay road maintenance fees and license fees like other companies. In short, on the one hand, reasonable compensation will be given, and on the other hand, they will be ordered to improve service efficiency.

Public Utilities Committee Meeting

[Another Dispatch] The Public Utilities Committee discussed the following proposals yesterday: (1) Request to amend the method of the Electrical Company collecting municipal construction donations, resolved: passed in principle, to follow the low-price standard and submit to the Finance Committee for review. If they are deemed unqualified, their use or sale may be suspended. Temporary motion: how to remedy the installation of electric lights in newly built houses that have not been issued building permits, resolved: if newly built houses have not obtained building permits from the Public Works Bureau, the Public Utilities Bureau should consult with the Public Works Bureau to handle.

Clearing Accumulated Coffins in the City; Health Bureau Sets Deadline for Removal from the City by Next Spring; Overdue Coffins Will be Cremated in Concentrated Areas

[Our Newspaper's Report] In order to improve the environmental sanitation of this city, the Health Bureau has decided to thoroughly clear the accumulated coffins in funeral homes, coffin storage places, and empty spaces in various districts of the city. The original deadline for the owners of coffins to remove them from the city was the end of the year, but it has now been extended to the end of March next year to allow the owners sufficient time. Coffins remaining in Shanghai after the deadline will be treated as ownerless and will be cremated in concentrated areas by district.

It is understood that more than 97,000 accumulated coffins in the city have been registered with the Health Bureau, and there are many others that have not been registered or are exposed in wasteland, estimated to total more than 100,000. Some of the ownerless coffins are mostly broken and decayed, with foul odors spreading everywhere. As a result, the district offices in each district have repeatedly requested the removal of the broken coffins. Now the Health Bureau has decided to handle the accumulated coffins in the entire city in a unified manner, adopting the most thorough method of cremation and implementing it within a time limit. In the future, the establishment of coffin storage places will be banned, and coffins placed in funeral homes will be limited to ten days. On the one hand, the government will establish a coffin transportation office to assist families in transporting coffins out of the urban area.

Since the decision on this measure, many owners of accumulated coffins have stated that they have no land and no money, making it difficult to relocate the coffins, and have called on the authorities to open more public cemeteries to allow for burial. However, according to the Health Bureau, the determination to clear the accumulated coffins has long been made, and the environmental sanitation of the majority cannot be affected by the difficulties of a few. As for opening more public cemeteries, it is not in line with the principle of promoting cremation and reducing public cemeteries in the new urban plan, and public cemeteries require land, estimated at 100 coffins per acre, then 100,000 coffins would require 1,000 acres. Moreover, there is an average of about 6,000 deaths per month. Not to mention that the municipal government lacks huge funds to purchase land, the value of land use is extremely uneconomical. At the same time, it is better for coffin owners to spend a sum of money to transport coffins to rural areas for burial once and for all than to store them in public houses and pay storage fees. Therefore, the Health Bureau hopes that coffin owners will comply with the deadline for removal.

Abundant Inventory, Tight Credit; American Goods Expected to Fall, Not Rise; Generally Believed That the Trend of Smuggling is Difficult to Eradicate

[Our Newspaper's Report] Since the announcement of the import permit system, the market price of American goods in this city has not fluctuated, and there is no phenomenon of customers crowding the American goods market. Industry insiders told reporters: there is a lot of American goods inventory in this city, and credit is very tight. Prices will only fall and will not rise. Business people believe that the implementation of the import permit system will not raise the market price of American goods in the short term, but if the implementation is effective, it will have an impact in the long term. However, whether this is the case depends on whether smuggling can be cracked down on. Most people do not believe that smuggling can be completely eradicated, because smugglers have very large backgrounds and strengths, and the methods of smuggling are extremely varied. Under the current new control methods, smuggling may even become more rampant. Under the control of this psychology, the market price of American goods will not fluctuate.

Cracking Down on Underground Money Shops; Rewarding Citizens for Reporting

The Social Affairs Bureau yesterday received an order from the Ministry of Finance to strictly crack down on underground money shops in the city and reward citizens for reporting. The original order stated: "Since prices have risen sharply, the market interest rate has increased along with commercial profits, resulting in the emergence of so-called "underground money shops," which illegally engage in banking business and provide high-interest loans, exploiting and profiting, disrupting finance, and fueling speculation. Although they have been repeatedly investigated and dealt with in accordance with the penalty rules for privately established banks and money houses stipulated in the Ministry's management methods for banks, ordered to suspend business, and fined, these types of money shops are mostly temporary combinations attached to residences or shops. It is already not easy to investigate and deal with them, and even if they are discovered, after being dealt with, they can still be established in another place and continue to operate as before. Their actions have clearly violated criminal law and should be severely punished according to law in order to ban and eliminate them.

Article 344 of Chapter 33 of the Criminal Law on fraud, breach of trust, and usury stipulates: "Whoever takes advantage of another's urgency, recklessness, or inexperience to lend money or other goods and obtains excessive profits that are clearly disproportionate to the principal shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than one year, detention, or a concurrent fine of not more than one thousand yuan." Article 345 stipulates, "Whoever habitually commits the crime in the preceding article shall be sentenced to imprisonment for not more than five years and may be concurrently fined not more than three thousand yuan." The reason why underground money shops can be rampant is that they take advantage of people's urgency, recklessness, and inexperience to achieve their goals of providing high-interest loans and illegally obtaining profits. In the future, all cases of this type that are discovered should still be reported to the Ministry and dealt with in accordance with the management methods for banks for the matter of unauthorized establishment of banks and money houses, and the part that violates criminal law should also send the criminals' credentials directly to the competent court for investigation according to law, in order to punish and warn. Please immediately transfer the order to all subordinates to strictly investigate these underground money shops and reward reporting in order to stop them, and should also issue a detailed announcement to all industries and businesses that if they need to finance funds, they should handle them at legally established banks and money houses according to proper procedures, or apply to local financial institutions (provincial and municipal bank branches) for small industrial loans in accordance with the regulations to avoid the exploitation of high-interest loans from illegal lenders (the following is omitted).

Principals and Professors Serve as Councilors

Council Asks the Judicial Yuan to Interpret Again

Regarding the matter that principals of public schools at all levels may not concurrently serve as provincial, county, or municipal councilors, the Ministry of Interior replied by telegram, "It has already been interpreted by the Judicial Yuan, and the Ministry has no right to correct it." The details have been recorded in various newspapers. Citizens throughout the city are paying close attention, especially councilors who are in a situation where they cannot hold both positions and are studying the issue of choosing. Alternate councilors also hope to be announced soon so that they can fill vacancies. However, yesterday, reporters visited the authorities of the Council. According to reports, the Council is preparing to ask the Ministry of Interior again to submit it to the Judicial Yuan for further interpretation. The reasons are four: (1) No democratic country has regulations that principals and professors may not serve as councilors. Since our country is a democratic country, it should be allowed to participate in elections. (2) Members of the Political Council and representatives of the National Assembly in this country are also allowed to participate as principals and professors, and there are no prohibitions. The nature of councilors is the same as that of members of the Political Council and representatives of the National Assembly, and there should also be no regulations that they cannot hold both positions. (3) Although principals of public schools are appointed, there is no clear distinction between the levels of Jianren and Weiren. Therefore, they cannot be generally regarded as civil servants. (4) In today's national advocacy of education to build the country and respecting teachers and valuing education, it cannot be regarded as wrong to have educational personnel represent the people.

Letter

Dear Editor, the section in your newspaper on the 18th of this month about the Wenzhou workers being beaten at the Rihui Port wharf is inconsistent with the facts. The dispute on that day was originally caused by Wenzhou worker Jiang Xueqin leading a crowd to destroy the fifth and sixth branches of our association, beating up staff members Zhang Xingkun and Xu Zhengyang, as well as the family members of the executive director of the association, and destroying all public property and the portrait of the national father. Zhang Xingkun is still lying in Guangci Hospital. Therefore, in addition to the Social Affairs Bureau handling this matter, our association has also filed a lawsuit in accordance with the law. We are afraid that the rumors are inaccurate. Please investigate and correct it. Shanghai Nanshi District Wharf Transportation Industry Workers Union.

Social Services Advocate for the Lonely Elderly, Poor, and Sick; Willing Philanthropists Are Encouraged to Donate Generously

Sixth Application: Nine out of Twelve Approved

On June 26, this column received a letter from Old Man Qingxia, which stated, "I am of meager virtue. My parents abandoned me when I was young. I am lonely and destitute, and I have tasted all kinds of hardships. I struggled to survive in society, worked hard, and avoided starvation... I have always admired your newspaper's enthusiasm for social services, so I dare to write a letter specifically to entrust you that if there are lonely elderly, poor, sick, and disabled civilians who are unable to make a living, I am willing to do my best to provide them with relief..." The next day, Old Man Qingxia handed over 500,000 Legal Tender and provided several suggestions. After being entrusted by this newspaper, it immediately formulated simple application rules and published them in this column on June 29. Subsequently, there were several applications every day. This column immediately followed the original intention of the old man and provided relief as appropriate. So far, for five months, five grants have been issued, benefiting more than 30 people. Later, thanks to the Jin Master of Jialin Loans, the colleagues of the Lianyizhang Firm, the colleagues of the Huamei Tobacco Factory, etc., who provided continuous assistance, the relief work became even larger. However, wailing spreads everywhere, and the severe winter is approaching. Those waiting to be fed are everywhere, and the fund has little left. We hope that enthusiastic people in society will work hard to donate generously so that the lonely elderly, poor, and sick can receive timely assistance, which is also a great good deed.

Twelve people applied for the sixth time, and nine have been approved. The difficult situations are as follows:

(1) Lu Yanwen wrote: "My husband, Zhang Linfa, unfortunately died of illness on June 21. His funeral was simple, leaving behind three children. Life is difficult. We rely on pawned items to make a living. Thinking about the future, I cannot help but shudder..." A relief fund of 100,000 was approved.

(2) Jiang Fen wrote: "My husband passed away in August of this year. There is an elderly aunt of 60 above and young children below. The family is poor. Now that the severe winter is approaching, we will not be able to avoid the cold and hunger!" A relief fund of 100,000 yuan was approved.

(3) Liu Furong wrote: "I am a civilian, Liu Furong. My family is poor, and I am suffering from illness. Life is extremely difficult. Please provide relief." A relief fund of 50,000 yuan was approved.

(4) Yang Shuxian wrote: "My husband passed away four months ago. His funeral was simple. Now I only rely on peddling to make a living. It is difficult for a family of several people to get a full meal. Recently, I have been plagued by illness and cannot work. I hereby write a letter to ask for relief." A relief fund of 50,000 yuan was approved. (To be continued).

[Note] Applicants approved above are requested to bring the receipt signed and sealed by the original Jia Chang Pu Bao after receiving the notification letter to the hall for verification and receipt.

Importer Registration Notice: Chen Changtong Explains in Detail to Various Banks

[Our Report] Chen Changtong, Director of the Secretariat of the Executive Committee of the Provisional Import Control Commission, convened a meeting with the responsible persons of various designated banks, both Chinese and foreign, at 1 p.m. yesterday on the fourth floor of the Bank of China. Mr. Chen gave a detailed explanation of the revised measures, implementing rules, and various application forms that had been issued. He also answered the questions raised by the various banks. The meeting adjourned around 4 p.m.

Most designated banks received the "Importer Registration Application Instructions" and four types of application forms issued by the Commission yesterday morning. However, due to printing issues, the number of copies issued was insufficient. Some banks have separately added their own printed copies according to the format. Once the printing is completed, applications can be accepted.

The "Importer Registration Application Instructions" list four items: (1) Importers should pay attention to Article 2 of the revised Provisional Measures for Import and Export Trade: "Importers must apply for registration with the Provisional Import Control Commission according to the type of business they operate. The registration method will be determined separately by the Provisional Import Control Commission. Applicants for import permits are limited to registered importers." (2) According to the provisions of the preceding article, the Commission has announced the following: "Any merchant with a fixed business address who was operating before December 8, 1941, or who started operating after the above date, and is currently a recognized agent of a foreign exporter, or can provide records within one year to prove that he has the ability to engage in import trade, may apply for registration." (3) Importers who wish to apply for registration in accordance with the provisions of Article 2 of the revised Provisional Measures for Import and Export Trade shall, within two weeks from the date hereof, complete Form AR-1 "If importing goods listed in Schedule (2), Form AR-1(A) must also be completed simultaneously." and submit it to the Secretariat of the Commission. (4) The deadline for application registration for importers in ports other than Shanghai may be appropriately extended.

Four Types of Application Forms

As for the four types of application forms: 1. The importer registration application form is Form AR-1. 2. The past import classification table (limited to goods in Schedule (2)) is Form AR-1(A). 3. The import permit application form for goods ordered before November 17, 1946, is exclusively for applying for goods in Schedule (1), and is Form AL-P2(I). This application form must be jointly approved by the Director of the Secretariat of the Executive Committee of the Provisional Import Control Commission and the Director of the Import Management Office. 4. The import permit application form for goods ordered before November 17, 1946, is for all goods other than those in Schedule (1), and is Form AL-P2(II). This application form must be approved by the Director of the Foreign Exchange Examination Department of the Central Bank.

All of the above forms must be completed in quadruplicate, and they are all import permit applications for goods ordered before November 17 of this year. As for the import permit application forms for goods ordered after that date, they have not yet been printed and distributed.

### Narrow Range of Trading in Gold, U.S. Dollar Continues to Fall

The gold market was extremely stable yesterday, with a very narrow trading range. It opened at 2.498 million and once rose to 2.505 million. The demand was sluggish, and the buyers felt slightly indifferent, resulting in a slight decline. The low price fell to 2.485 million. The Central Bank then allocated 60 bars at a price of 2.485 million. After 10 o'clock, it was more stable. At noon, it struggled around 2.49 million. The mood was slightly better in the afternoon. It was reported that the Shanghai dollar in Hong Kong market had fallen, and next-day settlement rose to over 2.5 million. As a result, it rose 10,000 compared to the previous close. Decorative gold was 66,000. Sycee silver and silver dollars were both flat. The black market money was still flat, and the interest rate was from 12% to 15%.

Foreign currencies were even more abundant and buying interest was difficult to stimulate. The black market for U.S. dollars started at 4,550 yuan and then fell again. At noon, it retreated to between 4,420 yuan and 4,470 yuan, a drop of 100 yuan compared to the previous close. There was less supply and demand for Hong Kong currency. ### Need for 50,000 Pieces, 60% Allocation, Cotton Yarn Supply and Demand Issues, Outports and Three Associations Request Assistance in Approval

Since the allocation of yarn for the reproduction industry, the Yarn Control Committee has been supervising the allocation of yarn. Recently, the Camel Hair Weaving, Canvas Weaving, and Ribbon Weaving Associations have requested the Yarn Control Committee to approve the allocation uniformly. It is reported that it is expected to be approved and will be included in the complex allocation for joint processing. These three industries have about 300 member factories, most of which are small and medium-sized. The demand for yarn is still limited. As for the dyeing, knitting, underwear, towel, blanket, handmade cotton weaving, and handkerchief industries, the supplementary declarations for yarn allocation by member factories have been compiled and reported. The Yarn Control Committee will hold a meeting today to consider it. According to sources from the complex allocation committee, the total amount applied for in November was originally 40,013 pieces. The Yarn Control Committee decided to temporarily approve 60%, totaling slightly more than 24,000 pieces, which will be allocated and sold in four installments. Tomorrow will be the fourth installment. The quantity was originally insufficient. In addition, there was too much 10-count coarse yarn and not enough fine yarn in the previous allocations. A few factories abandoned their allocations due to the urgent payment deadline and insufficient funds. The complex allocation committee failed to reallocate the allocations to the households with shortages, resulting in a shortage of fine yarn for most. As a result, there were still a few returns of fine yarn. The general factories are increasingly feeling the shortage of yarn. Those who rely on stockpiled yarn to supplement their needs are becoming increasingly scarce. If there is no remedy for the supply of yarn, the reduction in work in the reproduction industry is inevitable. Mr. Pan Shih-hao, the person in charge of the complex allocation committee, had already advised the various industries not to add more machines and not to rush to restore old factories that had been shut down. He also stated that although there was an allocation of cotton yarn, there was no way to supply machines that were added or restored. Recently, various reproduction industries are investigating their member factories in batches to strictly crack down on false reports. According to the latest statistics reported to the Yarn Control Committee, the six reproduction industries have a total of 1,889 member factories, with 66,722 various looms, requiring a total of 42,316 pieces of various counts of cotton yarn, equivalent to 51,526 pieces of 20-count yarn. If calculated at 60%, it would be more than 30,000 pieces per month. However, the yarn factories feel that this is too much, while the various reproduction factories still feel that it is not enough. How to coordinate and adjust the overall situation is a concern for all parties involved. In addition, the cotton yarn reproduction industries in the inland have also been requesting allocations one after another. It is reported that the Yarn Control Committee has been paying close attention to this. According to sources, since the reorganization of the yarn allocation mechanism, the output of 10-count yarn from the yarn factories has increased significantly, while the reproduction industry in this city does not need it. The cost of 10-count yarn is lower and the profit is higher. However, it is also a pity to reduce the equipment that can spin 20-count yarn to spin 10-count yarn.

Foreign Currency Not Allowed for Exchange, Central Bank Reaffirms Previous Prohibition

[Our Report] After the revision of the Measures for Import and Export Trade, the Central Bank issued Circular No. 61, notifying various designated foreign exchange banks to slightly revise the original regulations and abolish the provisions of Circulars No. 1, 26, 42, 45, and 54 (except paragraph 6). Circular No. 45 stipulated that foreign currency could not be used to offset foreign exchange. Now that the circular has been abolished, whether foreign currency can be used to offset foreign exchange in the future has attracted much attention. It is learned that the Central Bank has issued Circular No. 62 stating that after the cancellation of Circular No. 45, the designated banks are still not allowed to accept foreign currency to offset foreign exchange for non-import purposes that have not been approved by the Central Bank in advance.

Dispute Over Opening Yarn Market

Cloth Factories Having Difficulty Obtaining Yarn Prefer to Exchange Yarn for Cloth

[Our Report] There were still few transactions in the yarn market yesterday. Initially, Yong'an Yarn Factory planned to sell 100 pieces of 20-count Jincheng yarn at the official price, and Shenxin Yarn Factory also planned to open 100 pieces of yarn, limited to old customers who had previously traded with them. However, objections were raised by people in the industry, who believed that this was not a fair way. The two factories temporarily did not open up as a result. The external transactions were subject to the regulations of the Standing Bureau and did not open for business. A general customer help for those who are eager to handle goods, there is a great deal of money to buy no goods.

The cloth market is currently stable after Mayor Wu personally instructed the cloth industry representatives to pay attention to group prices. However, due to the small inventory, the price rises as soon as customers purchase it. General weaving factories have great difficulty obtaining yarn. They are unwilling to open sales in the market and often prefer to exchange yarn for cloth so that the raw materials will not be depleted. This kind of barter is really a last resort. Dyed cloth is also extremely tight due to the price of dyestuffs, so No. 190 Shilin has risen by another 4,000 to 5,000 yuan yesterday. Longtou fine cloth is currently priced at 92,000 yuan, Lanji fine cloth is priced at 90,000 yuan, and Sijunzi white printed poplin is currently priced at 98,000 yuan. Shilin cloth is priced at 145,000 to 146,000 yuan.

8,000 Tons of Rubber Allocated

Natural rubber, except for Hainan Island, has no domestic production. Since the victory, it has been controlled by the United Nations Rubber Allocation Committee and has not been directly imported into China. The Shanghai Rubber Products Association, concerned about the survival of China's rubber industry, submitted a request to the Ministry of Economic Affairs for the national monthly demand of 3,000 tons to be forwarded to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for negotiation. Recently, Hong Nianzu, chairman of the association, stated that he had received an instruction from the Ministry of Economic Affairs approving the telegraph from the Chinese Embassy in the United States: After contacting the United Nations Rubber Allocation Committee, the Chinese allocation is 8,000 tons until the end of this year, of which 5,000 tons are supplied by British and Dutch territories and Siam, and 3,000 tons are supplied by Vietnam. In the future, the raw materials of China's rubber products factories will no longer be in panic.

Black Market Oil at 2,000 Yuan, Already Discovered and Will Be Prosecuted

[Central News Agency] In order to suppress oil prices and stabilize people's livelihood, the municipal government has convened relevant parties to discuss and determine oil price limits and ordered the Social Affairs Bureau to strictly investigate black market oil prices and severely crack down on merchants selling oil on the black market in Jianzhang. It is learned that the Social Affairs Bureau discovered a black market oil sales invoice from Deyou Oil Shop on Caishi Street in this city yesterday, with a price of 2,000 yuan per catty. It has been dealt with according to law.

Soap Factories Suspend Production Seeking Tax Exemption

According to Liang Songling, chairman of the Shanghai Soap and Candle Industry Association, there are dozens of soap manufacturers in this city. Recently, due to high interest rates, large expenses, inconvenient transportation, and obstructed sales, business has been greatly affected. Recently, the government has also stipulated that soap manufacturers must pay taxes when leaving the factory, which the factories cannot afford. They have jointly requested the Executive Yuan to grant exemptions. Before approval is obtained, production will be temporarily suspended. However, the tax bureau must still collect taxes, so production has not been resumed.

The Canadian ship "Atholl Lake" set sail for Shanghai tonight carrying the gold. It is reported that this gold is intended to replenish the gold taken by the Japanese during the war.

South China Line Cargo Transportation Sluggish

[Our Report] According to shipping industry sources, the recent transportation situation on the South China Line, covering the provinces of Fujian and Guangdong, has become sluggish after the ban on the transportation of cotton yarn and cotton cloth. Shantou and Xiamen occasionally transport fertilizer and miscellaneous grains, while the goods from Guangzhou are all sporadic. Even those transported from Guangzhou are few. It is also learned that the cargo transportation on the North China Line has improved significantly recently. The bulk of the cargo is cotton yarn and cloth. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will run three ships this week. The Zhixin will sail to Tianjin today, and the Cai E will sail to Tianjin tomorrow. The Meilun is scheduled to sail to Tianjin on the 24th. In addition, the new ships Zizhong and Ding will sail to Qingdao on Sunday this week. It is reported that 2,000 tons of cotton from China Textile Corporation will be transported there. On the return journey, the ship will stop at Lianyungang to load salt for transport to the Yangtze River.

Mostly Settling Transactions, Hua Shares Show No Improvement

Yesterday was the last day for delivery of Hua shares. People's hearts were doubly troubled. Both buyers and sellers were mostly settling transactions. The market was extremely fluctuating, initially high and then low. At the opening in the morning, the prices of the shares were low. After Nos. 229 and 151 bought in, the buying intention on the surface was very strong, and the chips were surprisingly dry. The market gradually rose. After 10:45, it started to turn from firm to flat. The source of supply outside the market was gradually reported. Nos. 89, 4, and 151 sold. Even No. 111's efforts to buy Di Yong Yarn could not support it. Only around 11:30, Nos. 87 and 198 and others came in. After selling, No. 229 of Xian Yong Yarn re-entered. After the low, it was still easy to pull up. In the end, the surface and floating multiples competed to sell. The Xian Meiya fell miserably and retreated to a new low price. The Xian delivery price of Xinhe Yong Yarn occasionally showed an inverted phenomenon. As a result, compared to the previous close, Xian Yong Yarn, Xinhe, and Xinguang all saw slight declines, while Meiya and Jingfu each fell by half a percent. Qin Xing rose by half a percent alone because delivery was expected. Among the cold shares, China Textile, Match, and Huafeng rose slightly, while the rest all retreated slightly. There were no transactions for the delivery of Yonggong. The rest all fell slightly. In the afternoon, only cash transactions appeared. People's hearts were unstable. No. 229 sold and then entered again. After opening, the market once fell step by step. After Yong Yarn saw a low price of 562 yuan, retail investors seized the opportunity to maintain it. The surface helper then entered again. The chips were dry, and the market gradually increased. Nos. 38 and 176 strongly sold at high prices, but the buying was very strong, but it was only a slight struggle. As a result, compared to the previous close, Xian Yong Yarn, Meiya, Jingfu, and Xinguang retreated slightly, Xinhe rose slightly, and Qin Xing, supported by delivery, rose weakly by 10% alone. Among the cold shares, China Textile, Match, Cement, and Huafeng rose slightly, while the rest fell slightly to half a percent. There were no transactions for the delivery of Yonggong. The rest fell slightly to half a percent. The various shares outside the market fell slightly.

The market for foreign shares was stable yesterday. The rise and fall of the various shares was very small, and the process was mediocre. As a result, compared to the previous close, Yisha, British United, Yeguang, and Gangye Paper retreated slightly, while Shipping, Yipi, and Jardine Matheson were stable.

All brokers requested the Stock Exchange to provide evidence of delivery and commissions yesterday. It is learned that the Exchange promised to report the evidence money to the Ministry for instructions and that the reduction of commissions is still under consideration.

Export Material Loan Measures Approved by Four Banks, to be Handled by Three Banks and Two Bureaus

The Four Joint Offices, in order to assist the development of export trade, have successively approved the principles of packing loans and relaxed the methods for various banks and bureaus to undertake discount loans. Recently, in order to encourage exports and fully supply funds, the Four Joint Offices have approved the export material loan, re-pledge, and re-discount measures proposed by the Central Bank and notified various banks and bureaus to handle them. The measures are as follows:

(1) Participating Banks: The Three Banks and Two Bureaus and various foreign exchange designated banks are limited to applying for this re-pledge and re-discount.

(2) Loan Targets: Exporters who directly operate their own business and join the local industry association are limited to those who need financial accommodation to purchase export materials in the mainland or who request to handle discount loans for export materials in transit.

(3) Term: The original pledge shall not exceed 90 days. The term of the discount loan shall be determined according to the transportation situation. All Shanghai discount loans shall not exceed 25 days, except for Qingdao, Tianjin, Yichang, and Shashi. Chongqing shall not exceed 30 days. Other places shall not exceed 20 days.

(4) Limit: The original pledge loan shall not exceed 200 million yuan per household. The discount loan shall not exceed 300 million yuan per household. Those approved by the Four Joint Offices on a special case basis are not subject to this restriction.

(5) Collateral and Discount: The collateral is limited to the exporter's own export materials, and the discount is calculated at 70% of the cost.

(6) Interest: For the purpose of encouraging the export of materials, the original loan interest rate for this pledge discount loan shall not exceed 3% per month, and no other fees shall be charged. Various banks and bureaus shall re-pledge and re-discount to the Bank of China at 3/5 of the original loan interest rate. Various banks and bureaus should carefully handle this business. If the borrowed funds are not used for export, all interest shall be calculated twice from the date of the loan and the loan shall be recovered immediately.

(7) Discount Loan Exchange Rate: The original discount loan exchange rate shall be charged according to the local four banks and two bureaus' exchange rate table for remittances to various places. The re-discount loan exchange rate shall be calculated according to the bank's regulations.

(8) Re-Discount Discount: The re-pledge re-discount discount is calculated at 90% of the original loan.

(9) Application Procedures: Banks and bureaus that apply for re-pledge or re-discount shall submit the relevant documents to the local bank one by one. All procedures shall be handled in accordance with the bank's regulations.

White Coal Stops Falling and Turns Stable

In the coal market, the low price of white coal screen pieces has slightly increased, and the market situation is gradually stabilizing. Previously, due to the impending payment period for small-scale peers, those who were unable to purchase could only sell at low prices, and the market price once retreated. Today, because the payment period has arrived, the outflow of this batch of coal is scarce, and the market price has returned to a firm and quiet state. Since the source of Hongji chips for coal balls has been lacking and the allocation of goods from various factories has been reduced, the supply has been insufficient. Various coal shops are suffering from coping with it. The normal combustible coal balls have risen to 10,000 yuan per picul at the door.

The Jian gang opened up hundreds of bags of Diaoqing for 95,500 yuan, with no significant increase or decrease.

Nanyang Market, Britain and the United States Have Already Taken the Lead, National Goods are Too Expensive and Transportation is Difficult

[Our Report] A related person told the reporter: At present, the trade between our country and various parts of Nanyang is very sluggish. In the past, before foreign goods arrived in the Nanyang region, the temporary need was very urgent, and the standard requirements for goods were not high. Therefore, a considerable amount of our country's yarn and some daily necessities were transported to the South. But today, the situation is completely different. British and American goods have been imported into Nanyang in large quantities, and our country's yarn supply is insufficient. The high cost of goods, even if transported to Nanyang, is difficult to open up sales. Transportation is also a difficult problem. Currently, only the ships of the Java Shipping Company are sailing to Nanyang. Several weeks ago, a Nanyang merchant came to Shanghai to handle goods, but he still returned empty-handed, because the high prices in the Shanghai area made him afraid to start. As for the import of Nanyang goods, the number is also very small. Occasionally, some coconut oil and rubber are transported out, but the number is not large. Compatriots hope for national goods very much, but the motherland is really unable to satisfy their ardent hopes. Looking forward to Nanyang trade, it is difficult to be optimistic at present.

United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization (UNESCO) Conference Inaugurated by French President, Chinese Ambassador to France Qian Attends

[Reuters, Paris, 19th] The first General Conference of the United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization (UNESCO) was inaugurated today under the auspices of French President Pierre Pflimlin. More than 500 representatives from 26 countries attended. The flags of the 53 United Nations member states were displayed on the stage, in front of which sat 30 world-renowned educational leaders.

An Unprecedented Great Undertaking in World Education

British Chief Representative, Mr. Hardman, stated that this conference is an unprecedented and great undertaking for the world. Professor Rossi, Deputy Provost of the University of Paris, suggested establishing international colleges within major universities worldwide, directly controlled by UNESCO, to foster an international spirit among young people from various countries. In his opening address, President Pildour expressed regret over the absence of the Soviet Union, adding that UNESCO should become the foundation for mutual understanding among the United Nations, safeguard freedom of thought, develop cultural relations, and allow every philosophy and culture to develop freely in the world. It is reported that Bolivia and Syria have also ratified the charter of UNESCO, bringing the total number of participating countries in this General Conference to 28.

[Agence France-Presse, Paris, 19th] The UNESCO conference opened today at the Sorbonne Theatre here. The venue was adorned with the flags of participating nations. The entire diplomatic corps attended the meeting, including French Interim President and Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Pildour, Chinese Ambassador to France Qian Tai, Chairman of the UNESCO Preparatory Commission Huxley, Under-Secretary of the British Ministry of Education Hardman, French Minister of National Education Naicheren, President of the University of Paris Rossi, and numerous prominent scientists and writers.

France Pledges Support

First, the President of the University of Paris, Rossi, and the French Minister of National Education, Naicheren, delivered welcoming speeches, both pledging France's support as a backing for UNESCO. Subsequently, President Pildour delivered a welcoming address, strongly advocating that all countries should ratify the UNESCO agreement as soon as possible. He stated that the proponents of the so-called "new order" have now failed, and the task of those present is to inform the people, protect freedom of thought, and develop and guarantee cultural relations among nations. He earnestly requested that everyone should build barricades against any imperialistic attempts and prevent any opposition to the free exchange of ideas.

[United Press, Paris, 19th] The first General Conference of UNESCO opened today at the Sorbonne University here with a grand ceremony. French Minister of Education Naicheren delivered a welcoming speech on behalf of French Interim President and Foreign Minister Pierre Pflimlin, expressing the hope that the Soviet Union would join, which was met with cheers from the entire audience. Mr. Nai stated, "While welcoming you, I cannot help but feel concerned. Despite the splendor of the conference, one cannot forget an empty seat. We patiently await the day our absent friends will join us." Other speakers included the President of the University of Paris, Rossi, and the head of the British delegation, Hardman. The purpose of UNESCO is to promote cultural relations among countries and support world peace. To date, 41 countries have sent delegations or observers to participate. Although the Soviet Union is absent, Poland and Czechoslovakia have represented Eastern and Central Europe, and Yugoslavia has also sent observers.

China Cables Congratulations for a Successful Conference

[Our Newspaper, Nanjing, 20th] Mr. Zhu Jiahua, head of the Chinese delegation to the first General Conference of UNESCO, was unable to attend the conference in Paris due to other commitments. His position as head of the delegation has been delegated to Zhao Yuanren by special appointment of the National Government. Zhu, in his capacity as Minister of Education, cabled Chinese Ambassador to France Qian Tai to relay the following congratulatory message to the conference: "Due to official duties and the National Assembly, I am unable to attend, which I deeply regret. I sincerely wish the conference success and hope that the conference will make concrete decisions on communicating international culture to enhance mutual understanding among mankind and strengthen the factors of peace. I eagerly anticipate this!"

[Central News Agency, Paris, 19th] The first plenary session of the United Nations Educational, Cultural and Scientific Organization officially opened this afternoon at the "Su Peng Nai Circular Theater" of the University of Paris here. The venue was decorated with the flags of the United Nations. The representatives, deputy representatives, delegation members, other staff, and attending experts, diplomats, journalists, and photographers numbered over a thousand. Today's meeting was merely a welcoming ceremony, so only French Provisional President Pildour, the French Minister of Education, the head of the British delegation Hardman, and the Vice-President of the University of Paris, Rosai, delivered four brief speeches. There was also a musical program, featuring performances by the orchestra and the choir of the educational hall. The first business meeting is scheduled for tomorrow morning.

France and the Netherlands Sign Cultural Agreement

[Agence France-Presse, Paris, 19th] It has been officially announced that France and the Netherlands have recently signed an agreement here to promote cultural relations between the two countries. French Interim President and Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Pildour and Minister of Education Naicheren signed on behalf of France. On the Dutch side, the signatures were by Qi Ailian, head of the delegation attending the UNESCO conference, and the Dutch Minister to France, Busman.

U.S. College Student Enrollment Surges

Exceeds Previous High by Fifty Percent

[U.S. Information Service, Washington, 19th] According to the U.S. Education Office, the current number of students in U.S. universities and colleges exceeds two million, surpassing the previous high by fifty percent. The U.S. currently has 1,449 universities and colleges. The previous peak enrollment was 1,360,000 in 1939-1940. This year, there are 1,073,000 veterans enrolled, and the number of female students has also increased, totaling 667,000. According to the Education Office, due to the surge in student numbers, U.S. education authorities are facing a shortage of teaching staff and facilities.

Peking University Student Statistics: Law School Has the Most Students, Science School Has the Least

[Our Newspaper, Beiping, 20th] Peking University's various colleges, according to statistics of students allocated from the Southwest Associated University (Lian Da), students allocated from the Provisional University (Lin Da), and newly admitted students this year, excluding the College of Engineering, have a total of 2,650 students. The details are as follows: In the College of Liberal Arts, 289 students were allocated from Lian Da, 211 students were allocated from Lin Da, and 129 new students were admitted, totaling 630 students. In the College of Science, 90 students were allocated from Lian Da, 113 students were allocated from Lin Da, and 51 new students were admitted, totaling 254 students. In the College of Law, 250 students were allocated from Lian Da, 325 students were allocated from Lin Da, and 193 new students were admitted, totaling 768 students. In the College of Agriculture, no students were allocated from Lian Da, 340 students were allocated from Lin Da, and 30 new students were admitted, totaling 370 students. In the College of Medicine, no students were allocated from Lian Da, 569 students were allocated from Lin Da, and 59 new students were admitted, totaling 628 students. In summary, the five colleges of Liberal Arts, Science, Law, Agriculture, and Medicine have a total of 630 students allocated from Lian Da, 1,558 students allocated from Lin Da, and 462 new students.

Shanghai Education Bureau Begins Preparations for Students to Participate in Military Training

National Training Results Not Satisfactory

The Ministry of National Defense recently issued an order to all high school and above students nationwide to receive military training this year. Student families in this city expressed great concern. The reporter specially visited Mr. Li Ximou, Deputy Director of the Education Bureau, and was informed that the military training issue for high school and above students this year was only seen in the newspapers. The bureau has not yet received instructions from the Ministry of National Defense. However, in order to prepare all students in the city to receive military training, the bureau sent personnel to various schools to investigate the current situation of "National Training." The results were not satisfactory. The reason is that the instructors dispatched by the Ministry of National Defense to various schools to teach "National Training" mostly lack combat experience. Therefore, once military training is implemented, the actual ability of the instructors seems to be weak. Therefore, the bureau has prepared a document to submit to the Ministry of Education and forwarded to the Ministry of National Defense, requiring that teachers dispatched to various schools to teach military training in the future must have the following two qualifications: (1) Must have actual combat experience. (2) Must be graduates of the Central Army University. In this way, both knowledge and experience will be rich, and the foundation for students to receive military training can be laid.

However, there are many generals in the lineup, and there will be a tense and exciting performance when they meet the visiting team. Black and White have suffered consecutive defeats and will definitely strive to improve today. Although投篮好手萧华陀 Xiao Huatuo, a good shooter, cannot play due to injury, the entire team is already in normal condition.

Civil Administration Brief

Earnestly Protect Civil Servants, Administrative Officials May Not Be Dismissed Without Cause, City Government Orders Compliance Yesterday

The Municipal Government received instructions from the National Government, based on a presentation from the Ministry of Personnel through the Examination Yuan. The Personnel Work Review Conference regarding the protection of current civil servants passed a resolution to be sent to the Ministry of Personnel for reference when formulating the Protection Law. Before the promulgation of the Protection Law, please ask the National Government to reiterate the repeatedly decided orders to protect administrative officials, and notify all agencies to strictly comply. If there are any violations of laws and regulations, the Control Yuan should file an impeachment and punish them according to law. It has been repeatedly ordered that administrative officials in various agencies should not advance or retreat with political officials before the civil servant protection law is enacted, and civil servants appointed according to law should not be dismissed without cause. According to the previous report, it should be reiterated and earnestly implemented. After receiving the order, the Municipal Government has instructed to strictly comply and ordered its subordinates to comply accordingly.

Reassignment of District Chiefs in the Fourteenth District

Zhong Ketuo, the district chief of the 14th District (Zhabei), died of overwork and illness. The district affairs were temporarily handled by Deputy District Chief Sun Jingqi, who was appointed by the Municipal Government. It is now known that the vacancy has been filled by Wang Zhiping, the district chief of the 24th District, who assumed office in the district on the 19th of this month. He summoned all staff members for a discussion and inquired about the work situation of each section. It is said that District Chief Wang previously served as the deputy district chief of the 14th District and is quite familiar with the local situation. It is believed that local autonomy in Zhabei will be further promoted in the future.

Changes in Bao Chiefs in Various Districts

Weng Ziyu, the bao chief of the 3rd bao in the 23rd District (Wusong), resigned. The vacancy is temporarily filled by deputy bao chief Wang Baoli. Cai Guodong, the bao chief of the 20th bao in the 11th and 12th districts (Jiangning), was elected as a municipal councilor, relinquishing his position as bao chief. The bao convened a bao chief meeting and elected Cai Guo to fill the position and elected Zhang Yuankun as the deputy bao chief. Ye Jinfang, the deputy bao chief of the 34th bao in the 3rd District (Yimiao), moved away from the bao. The meeting of the jia chiefs voted to have Wang Jisheng fill the position. The district has respectively reported for approval.

Fifth District Requests Flour Distribution

The Fifth District (Taishan) Public Office, noting the large number of impoverished households in the areas under its jurisdiction in the southern part of the city, deemed them deserving of relief. They sent a letter to the Shanghai branch of the Relief Administration requesting the allocation of relief flour. It is reported that the branch has responded favorably. The survey forms for impoverished households, having been verified and completed by each Bao (neighborhood unit), have been submitted to the administration. The relief flour will be distributed according to procedure as soon as it is allocated by the Relief Administration. Furthermore, since its establishment, the cooperative in this district has actively promoted cooperative business. It is reported that a meeting of all councilors was recently held at the cooperative to discuss the development of business.
