"Collapse Wind" Strikes Hangzhou

— Special Correspondent Chu Yusheng

Hangzhou, 10th

After the victory, the complex and intricate nature of the takeover institutions caused unrest in domestic industry and commerce. Unexpectedly, domestic wars arose one after another, pushing this already fragile industry and commerce into a difficult predicament. It has now reached its most dangerous eve. In major cities across the country, the sound of merchant houses and firms collapsing is frightening and chilling. This is clearly bordering on the verge of industrial and commercial collapse. If no measures are taken to provide relief, then it will undoubtedly wither and die!

Collapse Wind Spreads Across All Industries

Hangzhou was originally a city that exported special products, such as silk, tea, and tung oil. In previous years, it not only won wealth for Zhejiang Province through the export of these special products, but also won back considerable honor in the international market. However, the export of special products after the war has become an extremely serious problem. Foreign markets already have substitutes or identical finished products. Domestic markets are plagued by chaos everywhere, coupled with currency devaluation, high costs, dumping of foreign goods, heavy profiteering, and onerous taxes, causing special products to encounter serious obstacles everywhere. As a result, they went from struggling to maintain to being unable to maintain. The number of merchant houses and firms that went from being unable to maintain to collapsing and being destroyed is indeed a considerable figure. This collapse wind has spread to every industry, with tea firms being the most affected. In thirty-six days, twenty-eight have already declared closure. Although there are no accurate statistics on other closed shops for the time being, there were twenty-four business units that applied to the city government for record and closure procedures in October, such as five in the cloth industry, five in the entertainment industry, one in the grain industry, one in the electrical machinery and silk weaving industry, two in the laundry and dyeing industry, one in the silk business, eight in the coarse paper industry, one in the sundry goods business, one in the preserved meat business, one in the native tobacco business, one in the timber rafting business, and one in the cotton weaving business. If we use monetary figures to illustrate its severity, it will be over 200,000,000,000 yuan.

Reasons for Tea Firm Closures

According to the operators, the reason for the tea firm closures is the government's levy of tea commodity tax. In its heyday, Zhejiang tea was originally subject to a special product tax levied by the province. Later, the provincial government abolished the special product tax in an attempt to revive the tea industry. Not long after, the Commodity Tax Bureau levied commodity tax again. When tea leaves were facing extreme difficulties with no way to export, they could not withstand the collection of this kind of tax, so they closed down one after another. Another reason is the exploitation of high-interest loans. Tea firm owners used funds obtained from high-interest loans to operate the tea business, which did not yield very high profits, and naturally felt somewhat strained. Conversely, if they used the funds for running a tea firm to make high-interest loans, they could worry much less. Therefore, the tea industry fears that it will not be able to restore its inherent prosperity for a while. The result of these tea firm closures will be that tea farmers will have fewer outlets for their tea leaves, and tea farmers will suffer extra blows and hardships. On the other hand, this nearly 100,000,000,000 yuan in funds will turn into floating capital, speculating and causing trouble in society.

In addition to the severe exploitation of high-interest loans and the two-pronged attack of the enticing allure of speculation causing closures of stores, another reason for the closure of many other firms is the decline in social purchasing power. The income of civil servants for a month is not enough to eat and dress warmly, let alone have the surplus to buy new things. The countryside is bankrupt, factories are precarious, and fellow farmers and workers also lack the ability to purchase. Moreover, due to the temptation of high-interest loans, even the remaining purchasing power that has been forgotten and left behind is transformed into floating capital, joining the ranks of high-interest loan businesses. Some of those who have obtained wealth from high-interest loans want to accumulate more and more, while others, although they buy some things, are ultimately a small minority. Therefore, in the market of Hangzhou City, many shops are seen every day decorating with lanterns and colored streamers, blowing and beating instruments, hanging large bargain flags with red silk and gold lettering, holding great sales from spring to summer, and then to autumn and winter throughout the year, but business is still far less lively than usual in previous years. If these great sales still do not make money, then the only option is to close down. The number of shops closing down in this way will increase more and more, the floating capital in society will accumulate more and more, and the production units will collapse more and more. Meanwhile, foreign goods are coming in continuously, both cheap and ingenious. It is unthinkable that our Chinese products can be sold abroad again, and because of the cheap and fine quality of foreign goods and the unrest in the domestic situation, it is also unthinkable that they can be sold to various parts of our country.

New Aspirations of the Business Community

Some say that to rescue China's current industry and commerce, only government banks can provide large amounts of low-interest loans. This goal is precisely the beautiful aspiration that the various business communities in Hangzhou are unanimously pursuing. However, if the government provides loans, the bright future after obtaining the loans is highly questionable. For example, when purchasing silkworm cocoons at high prices, the government sets a considerable price, but cocoon merchants still clamor that it is not high enough, while in reality, the purchase price is often less than the government-set price. The reason for this is because the bank has loans, and the government lends to the cocoon merchants according to the set price. The cocoon merchants use a small amount of money to buy cocoons, and use the other money for other purposes. - These purposes are presumably for things like high-interest lending. Therefore, in order to ensure that these loans are indeed used in the industrial and commercial sectors, and that they are indeed for seeking industrial and commercial revival, there must be strict investigation, meticulous lending, and after lending, there must also be thorough assessment. Some people say, if these funds are lent out, won't inflation increase further and the currency depreciate further? I believe that as long as these many loans are directly lent to production units, and truly make one yuan produce the effect of one yuan, then it can still revive a portion of industry and commerce.

Grand Old Slogans

In addition, we would like to propose a grand old slogan that has been ineffective for decades, which is "Chinese people should use Chinese goods." First, we must cultivate a national mentality of loving domestic goods. I remember that before the war, in the Hongkou area of Shanghai, there was a Japanese child who wanted to buy a box of cigarette lighters. He went to a Chinese shop, and the shop assistant told him: "We have Chinese lighters, which are cheaper and better than Japanese ones. Why don't you buy a box to try!" But the child shook his head and left. He still went to a Japanese shop to buy a Japanese lighter to take back. This story can alert us, can awaken us. Our industry and commerce are so fragile today, and only by doing this, only by doing this, can we find a solution.

Encouraging the Export of Special Products

Hangzhou is a city for transporting and selling special products, and Zhejiang is a key area for agricultural special products. If these many special products cannot be transported and sold abroad for a while, then everyone will collapse. Therefore, the government should invest heavily and reluctantly encourage the export of special products, even at a loss. For example, the tea firms and shops have closed down as many as twenty-eight due to the increase in commodity tax, which is worth the government's consideration.

Need for Expert Research

We may also invite experts to conduct detailed research on these many special products and invent various other daily necessities, just like Germany during the war, which was able to turn [illegible] into bread substitutes, and the United States after the war, which was able to make socks, leather shoes, leather bags, etc. from plastic (Plaztic), which can be said to be the result of research.

The collapse wind of shops and firms has fiercely struck Hangzhou, a city for transporting and selling special products. We don't know when this strange wind will stop. We can only automatically strengthen and consolidate our houses, so as not to have this strange wind blow all our people and things into the ocean, and be swallowed by the waves.

The Re-education of Over Two Million Taiwanese Compatriots - Civic Training in Taiwan

— He Minxian

Taiwan Air Mail, 12th

On this National Day of historically great significance, on the treasure island of Taiwan, is the first day that 2,394,685 male and female youth citizens successively began to receive "re-education". It has now been closed for training for more than a month. Regarding the unprecedented training work of this large-scale and universal nature held in the province, it can be regarded as unprecedented and truly an initiative. According to the relevant authorities, the training motivation, goals, and the content and process of the work carried out are as follows:

Understanding the Actual Situation of the Country

The motivation for the Taiwan Provincial Government to re-educate these two million citizens is based on the fact that Taiwan Province was under Japanese rule for fifty-one years in the long years of shackles. Japan has consistently implemented a policy of isolation, gradually alienating compatriots in this province from the motherland. Now that the province has been restored for almost a year, but none of us can deny the necessity for compatriots in this province to have a deep understanding of everything about the motherland. The greatest purpose of this event is to exercise civil rights and hope to build a sound foundation for our local autonomy. Then, following the instructions of Chief Executive Chen, adult training should be held quickly, using a simple and clear method to tell them about the history, geography, and customs of the country, so that they can understand the actual situation of the country. Therefore, the "Taiwan Provincial Civic Training Committee" was organized to be responsible for hosting and promoting everything. Because the educational level and law-abiding habits of compatriots in this province are higher than any other province in the mainland, as long as they have a deep understanding of everything about the motherland in the future, they will definitely make unparalleled contributions to the country and the nation!

Six Training Objectives

Its training objectives are six: (1) Strengthen the understanding of the Chinese nation, (2) Deeply understand the current situation of our country, (3) Actively promote the essence of the Three Principles of the People, (4) Fully develop the virtues of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, and peace, (5) Comprehensively and universally promote government decrees, (6) Train popular teaching.

Three Basic Organizational Layers

The basic organization for promoting this training work is divided into three layers of agencies: provincial, county (city), and township (town). Such as (1) At the provincial level: organize a civic training committee, with the civil affairs office, education office, propaganda committee, and other relevant personnel as members, to preside over civic training matters throughout the province, and with Director Zhou Yi'e of the civil affairs office as the chairman; (2) At the county and city levels: also establish a committee with the county mayor as the chairman; (3) At the district and township (town) levels: assign the district chief and township chief as supervisors.

Two Training Methods

As for the training methods, according to their nature, they are divided into classroom-style training, that is, setting up "civic training lecture halls," and the general extensive training, that is, "social civic training." (A) Civic training lecture halls - using local schools, churches, Sun Yat-sen halls, and other public places in each village and neighborhood as the hall site. (If there is a lack of teachers, one lecture hall may be set up jointly by two to three villages and neighborhoods. In the first phase, each household designates one male or female person aged 20 to 30 to participate. If the venue permits and there is no difficulty in recruiting teachers, two classes for men and women can be set up separately. The training period for each phase is set for one month, two hours each day, with the time arranged so as not to hinder their work. (B) Social civic training - using local cinemas and theaters as lecture halls for implementing social civic training, broadcasting slides and lectures for 30 minutes before each screening, or using other methods that arouse their interest. At the same time, broadcasting civic training courses on the radio for 30 minutes every day.

Eight Training Subjects

The subjects of the civic training lecture hall are divided into two major departments: political and Sinicization. The former includes the promotion of government decrees and the application of the four powers, while the latter includes the understanding of history and geography and the inculcation of party doctrine. The detailed content includes twelve items: (1) Mandarin, (2) Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, (3) President's speeches, (4) New Life Movement, (5) History and geography, (6) Essentials of local autonomy, (7) Overview of the province's administration, (8) Current affairs explanation, (9) Laws and regulations explanation, (10) Physical education, (11) Music, (12) Others. Judging from the content of the above-mentioned teaching materials, they are the minimum that a citizen must understand. If everyone can receive good training, they will definitely gain a lot when the term expires. Currently, the association has compiled and printed 100,000 copies of this textbook, which are responsible for distributing them to meet their needs.

Teachers Recruited Locally

Due to the limited funding and the difficulty of recruiting teachers and talents, the teachers of each subject in the civic training lecture hall are all recruited locally, and the committee in each county and city hires local elementary and secondary school teachers, administrative and autonomous personnel, party and state workers, government decree propaganda personnel, local people, and others who have a basic understanding of the training subjects. As for the broadcasters or lecturers of social civic training, they are hired by the provincial, county, and city civic training committees, hiring those who are knowledgeable and have teaching experience. The above-mentioned personnel are all honorary positions, and only provide spiritual encouragement to assist in the development of public messaging work.

Strict Assessment of Merit and Demerit

In order to understand the promotion situation of each county and city this time, prepare a reference for the second phase of the plan to be launched next year, and to ensure that this training does not waste time, manpower, and material resources, and can achieve satisfactory results, the special commissioner dispatched inspectors to 17 counties and cities throughout the province in separate areas. It is expected that after this inspection, many valuable opinions will be contributed, and it will enable us to better understand the actual truth of this training work. As for the rewards and punishments, they are divided into three aspects:

(1) List the civic training work as one of the annual assessments of the county mayors and mayors of each county and city, and the district chiefs and township chiefs who are responsible for presiding over the work.

(2) If a trainee is absent without reason, violates the rules of the lecture hall, or engages in other improper conduct, a warning will be given according to the severity of the circumstances, or the names of those who are absent will be posted, and they will be punished with labor service (work service) for one to two days (and even after receiving the aforementioned punishment, they must still be forcibly ordered to attend the training.) If the circumstances are serious, they may be handed over to the local police authorities for severe punishment in accordance with the rules for punishing police offenders. As for trainees with excellent character, who abide by the rules, and who have excellent test results, they will also be given commendations.

(3) If a part-time teacher in charge of the lecture hall serves conscientiously, teaches diligently, and has excellent results, they will be given a commendation and recorded a merit, and will be listed as one of the annual assessments of the original service unit.

Progress Ascends Sequentially

The civic training subjects are as mentioned above. As for the content and materials, they are completely aimed at citizens with the level of graduation from national schools, and the writing examples are as simple as possible. At the same time, teachers of each subject can also supplement them at any time, and its progress is sequential. Taking the subject of "Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings" as an example, it is listed in the first week, and the arrangement for the six days is as follows: on the first day, first talk about the biography of Dr. Sun Yat-sen; on the second, third, fourth, and fifth days, continue to buy about the nationalism, democracy, and people's livelihood in the Three Principles of the People; on the fifth day, talk specifically about the psychological construction in the "Strategy of National Reconstruction"; on the sixth day, continue to talk about the political construction of the "Industrial Plan" and "National Construction Outline." The other seven weeks are used for [illegible] utterances, New Life Movement, and local autonomy, and each subject is also distributed equally in the same way as above, in an orderly manner, so that trainees can get a complete concept of each issue.

Hope to Work Together

The civic training held in Taiwan Province this time is very important to the psychological construction of compatriots throughout the province. If we want to build a new Taiwan based on the Three Principles of the People, we must pay more attention to their psychological construction. However, this arduous task requires the joint efforts of the government and the people. Citizens are the masters of the country. If they lack even the minimum knowledge and ability that a citizen should have, then it will greatly reduce the power to build the country. Here, I sincerely hope that people of insight from every corner of Taiwan will come together to assist the local government in completing the government's great plan to implement civic training, and that everyone will embrace the spirit of "those who know first awaken those who know later" and "those who are aware first awaken those who are aware later," and give them practical help at all times to achieve brilliant results.

Hongshanzui, with its dangerous terrain, is located outside Dihua City. The Jade Emperor Temple is built on the mountain. (Photo by our reporter)

An Overview of Xinjiang (Part Four)

— Special Translation by Our Newspaper's Translation Department

If Chairman Zhang Zhizhong wishes to regain the confidence of the indigenous people of Xinjiang Province, he must overcome two crucial difficulties. First, he must obtain economic assistance from Nanjing to alleviate Xinjiang's declining economic situation, with the construction of roads and improvement of transportation being the most pressing concern. Second, he must eliminate the widespread communist propaganda. Undoubtedly, the Soviet Union is extraordinarily concerned about Xinjiang's political future.

To restore prosperity and stability to Xinjiang, General Zhang Zhizhong has specially hired ten of China's most progressive engineers to go to Dihua to plan a development scheme for Dihua on Zhang's behalf.

Finally, Zhang urgently needs a team of well-trained and physically strong soldiers who can withstand the harsh climate of the mountains and deserts, to replace the poorly trained recruits currently stationed at key locations in Xinjiang.

General Medical Conditions

Due to a lack of medicine, doctors, and hospitals in Xinjiang Province, public health conditions are extremely poor. Provincial officials have stated that unless relief is provided before the height of winter, the two epidemic diseases of typhus and cholera will likely cause disaster for the indigenous Hui people. In reality, these two Asian epidemics are currently relatively mild; the diseases with the highest and increasing mortality rates in Xinjiang are smallpox, dysentery, malaria, syphilis, and typhoid fever.

According to estimates by health authorities, the infant mortality rate in Xinjiang Province exceeds 70%, mostly due to smallpox and dysentery.

A severe typhus epidemic is spreading in the mountainous pastoral areas surrounding Dihua. Unless serum and preventive agents such as DDT are rushed from eastern China, the epidemic is feared to soon spread to Dihua.

Dihua, with a population of 100,000, has only two hospitals: one general hospital with 400 beds and one mental hospital with 40 beds. Both are very poorly equipped. The entire Xinjiang Province has a total of ten hospitals with 1,100 beds. The provincial population is estimated by the Mountain State government to be 4 million, while the Hui people themselves claim it is over 7 million. However, this vast population receives very little medical assistance.

According to health authorities, only three tons of medicine have been shipped to Xinjiang Province from eastern China since 1943. It is said that UNRRA (United Nations Relief and Rehabilitation Administration) allocated medicine to Xinjiang Province two years ago, but due to a lack of transportation, this medicine is still held up in Kunming, Chongqing, and Nanjing.

Xinjiang urgently pleads with UNRRA and CNRRA (Chinese National Relief and Rehabilitation Administration) to rush serum, sulfur preparations, DDT, and other medicines to rescue the critical public health situation there. A single plane can carry enough medicine to avert the crisis. This gives UNRRA and CNRRA an opportunity to prove the noble value of their relief work.

Due to the political situation created by the successful Hui rebellion, UNRRA or CNRRA medicine is best delivered directly to Hui leaders, without accompaniment by American or Chinese officials; otherwise, the Hui people will refuse to accept it.

The Manas River is the military boundary separating China from the northwestern areas controlled by the rebels. Here, it symbolizes the daunting task that China undertakes in political and economic construction. The "Great Western Bridge" over the Manas River, before it was destroyed by floods this June, was the only road bridge connecting the inland areas of deserts and mountains with the fertile northwestern border of the new province. Now, only two empty, three-earthen-pillar bridge abutments remain, facing each other on the banks of the Manas River. According to a government spokesperson, the authorities are not yet prepared to rebuild the bridge. If this bridge remains unbuilt, it is difficult to imagine restoring friendly relations between the National Government in Dihua and the rebel government in Yining. Telegraph and telephone lines between Dihua and Yining have been cut off since the Hui rebellion from September 19, 1944, to January 19, 1946, and have not been reconnected.

During this summer's low tide, some cargo trucks carrying Soviet cloth, candy, and cigarettes were able to wade across the Manas River to Dihua. However, the winter storms have arrived, foreshadowing that this limited transportation will also be cut off. Therefore, until next summer, the only transportation line between China and Yining will depend on the irregular flights of Soviet airline transport planes. China is striving to restore the territorial integrity of its largest and most remote province, and it seems that even geography is working against China.

If General Zhang Zhizhong, the chairman of Xinjiang Province, wishes to regain the confidence of the four million Hui people of Xinjiang, he must restore commerce in the heart of Xinjiang. In fact, the majority of Xinjiang's exportable products grow in the fertile three northwestern regions, namely Yili, Tarbahatai, and Altai.

Dihua, historically the administrative center of Xinjiang, is now striving to maintain its position as a trading post for camel caravans from northern and southern Xinjiang. Currently, apart from cosmetics, cigarettes, tea, and a small amount of cloth, almost no goods are shipped from mainland China. Therefore, Dihua must obtain various supplies from the rebel government in Yining. However, Dihua has nothing that Yining needs except tea, cosmetics, and cigarettes.

Dihua urgently needs goods produced in Yining, such as grains, beef, mutton, animal hides, rice, fruit, gasoline, and gold. However, even if the Manas River Bridge is rebuilt and these commodities can be transported, Dihua ultimately cannot compete with Kazakhstan, because the latter has excellent roads, abundant consumer goods, and machinery, which are needed by the Hui people of the northwestern region but cannot be supplied by the Chinese authorities. What the entire Xinjiang Province urgently needs are textile factories to weave local cotton and wool into cloth.

When Sheng Shicai ousted Soviet industries in 1942, he used US$4.2 million to purchase a modern aircraft manufacturing plant from the Soviet Union, intending to convert it into a textile factory. Sheng also used US$500,000 to purchase American textile machinery from a company in Shanghai, but this machinery has not yet been delivered. As a result, millions of indigenous people and thousands of Chinese soldiers in the new province are left without warm clothing, preparing to endure another harsh winter. There is a surplus of cloth in neighboring Soviet territory, but it cannot be obtained for the following two reasons:

First, the Yining government fears opposing the transportation of this cloth to Dihua.

Second, since Sheng Shicai closed the western gate of the new province, the Soviet Union has not concluded any commercial treaty with the new province.

Unless cloth is rushed here from the mainland within a month, traversing 2,000 miles of desert roads, millions of people and thousands of Chinese troops in the new province will be in danger of freezing and starvation.

National Defense Highway

Recognizing the importance of defending its Central Asian frontier, China has allocated 30 billion Legal Tender (Chinese currency) to build a military highway network to connect the vast remote province of Xinjiang with mainland China. With no preparations currently being made to repair the war-torn roads in the interior provinces, this costly project is worthy of attention. This new national defense highway trunk line runs from Lanzhou in northern Gansu, crosses the border of Qinghai, and reaches Dihua, the capital of Xinjiang Province, for a total length of one thousand seven hundred li. The section from Lanzhou to Duolan, about three hundred and fifty li, has been completed. From Duolan, it must cross the branches of the Kunlun Mountains, pass through the desolate marshes of the Qaidam Basin, then cross the snow-covered Altyn Tagh Mountains, penetrate the southern edge of the Taklamakan Desert, and meet the ancient caravan route in Qakilik. It crosses the desert to Kucha, where it quickly ascends the mountain road across the Tianshan Mountains and goes straight to Dihua. The necessity of this arduous undertaking lies in the following facts: Currently, the only connection between Xinjiang and mainland China is the ancient Silk Road from Lanzhou, passing through the Xingxing Gorge mountain pass on the eastern side into Xinjiang Province, taking the route through Hami. This medieval road has been frequently attacked by bandits in recent months, posing a dangerous risk from guerrilla bandits who often come and go in the mountains along the Outer Mongolian border. The main purpose of this Lanzhou-Dihua highway is to prevent the isolation of Dihua, the key western fortress of China. Its strategic importance is no less than that of the motor road that the Soviet Union is now completing outside the western border of Xinjiang. This road is located between Stalinabad and Khorog, passing through plateaus higher than 13,000 feet in the Pamir Mountains. However, the difference is that the Soviet Union is using modern road-building machinery, while China must build the road manually, in the harsh winter. (The End)

Datong Medical Center for Soldiers (Special Correspondent Hang Zhou)
